Nice. I’ve got the full picture now.

I’ll give you 3 things in this message:

1️⃣ What you already have in place
Core architecture
Neon DB schema — You’ve already designed and (per your own doc) built the full Neon core:

users, credit_transactions, jobs, cleaner_earnings, payouts, job_photos, messages, app_events, plus supporting tables for disputes, payment_failures, KPIs, notifications, etc.

Implementation guide is a full phased system plan:

Phase 0: repos + infra doc

Phase 1: Neon tables + indexes + seed data

Phase 2: Base44 pages (CleanerSchedule + CleanerJobWorkspace) wired to Neon

Phase 3: App Events Ingest + core n8n workflows

Phase 4: Credits & approval logic

Phase 5: Payments, payouts, media

Phase 6: Refinement & admin

Base44 / product layer
Base44 entities cover the entire marketplace surface:

CleanerProfile, ClientProfile, Booking, Review, PhotoPair, SupportTicket, Credit, Event, Payment, Payout, RecurringBooking, Dispute, Message, CleanerAnalytics, etc.

Credit & escrow logic is defined at the entity level:

Credit entity is the ledger; ClientProfile.credits_balance is the live balance.

Booking has escrow_credits_reserved and all the “credit escrow” semantics are spelled out (reserve on booking, final charge, refunds).

Reliability & pricing are specified:

Reliability_score & tier driven automatically from booking + review events, with detailed metrics like attendance, punctuality, cancellation rate, photo proof rate, etc.

Pricing driven by CleanerProfile hourly credit rates, snapshot into Booking at accept (snapshot_base_rate_cph, etc.).

Stripe + n8n automations
You actually have a pretty complete Stripe automation stack:

01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest

n8n Webhook at stripe/webhook that passes events into the router workflow.

02 – Stripe Event Router

Normalizes event type and routes to the correct processor:

payment_intent.succeeded → 03

payment_intent.payment_failed → 04

charge.refunded → 05

charge.dispute.created → 06

charge.dispute.closed → 07

payout.paid → 08

payout.failed → 09

03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

Normalizes payment intent payload + metadata (pt_event_type, pt_client_id, pt_expected_credits).

Calculates credits (either from pt_expected_credits or amount_cents / 100).

Finds client by Stripe or PT ID, updates clients.credit_balance, inserts a credit_transactions row, and (optionally) calls a “Notify Client of Credit Purchase” workflow (currently disabled with placeholder ID).

04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

Extracts failure info and inserts into payment_failures, linked to the client, with error code/message.

05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

Extracts refund details, finds client, calculates credits_refunded (from metadata or amount), writes a negative credit_transactions row, and updates clients.credit_balance back up.

06 – Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor

Extracts dispute payload, finds job/client/cleaner by payment intent / charge / PT IDs, inserts into disputes, and flags the job as dispute_status = 'open'.

07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

Updates the disputes record with status, closed_at, metadata/evidence, and syncs jobs.dispute_status.

08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

On payout.paid, finds the payout row, marks payouts.status = 'paid', sets paid_at, updates cleaner lifetime_earnings_cents and last_payout_at.

09 – Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor

On payout.failed, marks payouts as failed, stores failure code/message, and flags the cleaner with has_payout_issue = TRUE.

Jobs, events, KPIs, backups
Job Lifecycle Event Router (10)

Webhook /job/events, normalizes job event payload, routes by event_type (job_created, job_assigned, cleaner_checked_in/out, job_completed, client_approved/rejected, cancellations, no-shows, etc.), and logs each branch (currently logging-only handlers).

Daily KPI Aggregator (11)

Nightly job inserting a row into kpi_daily aggregating credit sold/used, revenue, payouts, jobs created/completed, new clients/cleaners.

Daily Backup & Snapshot (12)

Cron job that inserts a record into backup_runs as a placeholder for a future full backup/snapshot process.

There are also job-specific workflows (ingest, lifecycle, photos, notes/checklists, notifications, payouts) from all the JSONs you uploaded; they line up nicely with the Implementation Guide phases and Base44 entity semantics.

Meta: your own status doc
Your “to do list + completion %” doc already recognizes:

✅ Full Neon DB schema is built and aligned

✅ 12 n8n workflows exist (but some still need SQL alignment/wiring)

✅ React + Base44 app with all main pages exists (clients, cleaners, admins, bookings, reliability, payouts, disputes, analytics, messaging, etc.)

✅ December + launch content scripts are written

✅ JSON schema docs are ready to feed n8n AI for SQL generation

You’re not at “idea” stage; you’re at integration + hardening.

Yes, 100%. Let’s turn that “Stripe ↔ n8n ↔ Neon isn’t fully hardened” section into a clear implementation guide you can follow (or hand to a freelancer).

I’ll break it into:

Prep & schemas

Idempotent ingest + router (01 + 02)

Payments: payment_intent.succeeded + failures (03 + 04)

Refunds: charge.refunded (05)

Disputes: open/close (06 + 07, and the empty stub)

Notifications: fix the placeholder in 03

Idempotency & duplicate webhook test plan

1️⃣ Prep: Make sure the “ground” is solid
1.1 Confirm Stripe idempotency tables exist
In Neon, you should already have:

stripe_events (for raw events + idempotency)

Optional payment_intents table

credit_transactions with idempotency_key + unique index

Action:

Run in Neon (or check with \d):

\d stripe_events;
\d payment_intents;
\d credit_transactions;
Confirm:

stripe_events.id (PK, text), type, payload jsonb, handled boolean exist.

credit_transactions.idempotency_key has a unique index where NOT NULL.

If they’re missing, run the migrations from the Stripe + Credit System sections of your canon.

1.2 Confirm environments + credentials
In n8n, you have a Postgres credential named exactly: PureTask Postgres.

Stripe webhooks (test mode) are pointed to:

Either the verifier → then to n8n /webhook/stripe/webhook, OR

Directly to n8n’s stripe/webhook path defined in Workflow 01.

2️⃣ Harden 01 + 02: Ingest + Router with idempotency
2.1 Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest
Goal: Every Stripe event is stored once, marked handled once, and routed safely.

In n8n:

Open 01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest.

Check nodes (matches your doc):

Node 1: Webhook stripe/webhook (POST).

Node 2: Extract Body/Headers (keeps stripe-signature).

Node 3: Verify signature (if using verifier, this might just trust X-Stripe-Verified).

Node 4: “DB: Insert Event” (Postgres):

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id) VALUES (...) ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING;

Node 5: (Optional) Upsert payment_intents.

Node 6: HTTP Request or Execute Workflow to 02 - Stripe Event Router.

Final Node: “DB: Mark Event Handled”:

UPDATE stripe_events SET handled = TRUE, handled_at_utc = now() WHERE id = :event_id;

Make sure ordering is:

Insert stripe_events → (if not already handled) → Route → Mark handled.

If you don’t yet have the “skip if already handled” behavior:

Add an extra Postgres node “Check if handled” right after Insert Event:

SELECT handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Use an IF node:

If handled = true → go straight to response (no-op).

If handled = false → continue to router.

This gives you idempotency at the event level: rerun of same webhook won’t redo money moves.

2.2 Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router
Goal: Cleanly route to the correct downstream flow.

Open 02 - Stripe Event Router and:

Confirm the Switch/IF on event.type has branches for at least:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

payout.failed

For each branch, make sure it calls the correct workflow:

payment_intent.succeeded → 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

payment_intent.payment_failed → 04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

charge.refunded → 05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

charge.dispute.created → 06 - Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor (the real one, NOT the empty stub)

charge.dispute.closed → 07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

payout.paid → 08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

payout.failed → 09 – Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor

If 02 is still pointing to placeholder HTTP URLs (https://REPLACE_ME/...) from earlier docs, change those nodes to Execute Workflow and select the actual local workflows.

3️⃣ Payments: payment_intent.succeeded & payment_intent.payment_failed
3.1 Workflow 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor (credits purchase)
Goal: When Stripe says “success”:

Insert/update payments

Insert a credit_transactions row with type purchase

Increase client’s credit balance (or via view/trigger)

(Optionally) enqueue a notification

From your todo doc target:

“Upsert into payments… insert into credit_transactions with type='purchase'… update clients.credit_balance …”

Step-by-step in 03:

Node: Extract Payment Data (Code)

Already there: extracts event.type, payment_intent.id, amount, currency, metadata including pt_client_id and pt_event_type.

Confirm it sets:

payment_intent_id

amount_cents

stripe_customer_id

pt_client_id (from metadata, if present)

pt_expected_credits (if you’re using that)

Node: Guard on payment_intent.succeeded

IF node → only continue when event_type == 'payment_intent.succeeded'.

Node: Find/Upsert Client

Postgres node:

SELECT * FROM clients WHERE stripe_customer_id = $1 OR id = $2 LIMIT 1; using stripe_customer_id + pt_client_id.

Node: Upsert payments

Postgres node that UPSERTS a payments row keyed by stripe_payment_intent_id:

INSERT INTO payments (
  stripe_payment_intent_id,
  client_id,
  amount_cents,
  currency,
  status,
  last_event_type,
  created_at,
  updated_at
)
VALUES (
  $1, $2, $3, $4, 'succeeded', 'payment_intent.succeeded', NOW(), NOW()
)
ON CONFLICT (stripe_payment_intent_id)
DO UPDATE SET
  amount_cents = EXCLUDED.amount_cents,
  currency = EXCLUDED.currency,
  status = 'succeeded',
  last_event_type = 'payment_intent.succeeded',
  updated_at = NOW()
RETURNING *;
Use payment_intent_id, client id from previous node, amount_cents, currency.

Node: Compute credits purchased

Code node:

const item = $input.item.json;
const expected = item.pt_expected_credits;

let credits = expected;
if (!credits) {
  // fallback: 1 credit per $1
  credits = item.amount_cents / 100;
}

return [{
  json: {
    ...item,
    credits_purchased: credits,
    // Good idempotency key: "pi:<pi_id>:purchase"
    idempotency_key: `pi:${item.payment_intent_id}:purchase`
  }
}];
Node: Insert credit ledger row

Use the canonical credit_transactions schema + idempotency.

INSERT INTO credit_transactions (
  client_id,
  job_id,
  type,
  amount_credits,
  note,
  idempotency_key
)
VALUES (
  $1, NULL, 'purchase', $2, 'Stripe credit purchase', $3
)
ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key)
DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
If you’ve implemented the plpgsql helper create_credit_tx(...) that uses advisory locks + idempotency, call that instead.

Node: Update client balance (if you use a mirror column)

If you’re still manually mirroring balance on clients.credit_balance (or users.wallet_credits_balance):

UPDATE clients
SET credit_balance = credit_balance + $1,
    updated_at = NOW()
WHERE id = $2
RETURNING *;

4️⃣ Refunds: charge.refunded → Wallet reversal
Workflow 05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor
You’re very close here. It already: extract, guard charge.refunded, find client, compute credits, insert credit_tx, update balance.

Hardening steps:

Confirm the IF Is charge.refunded? is correctly checking the type.

Confirm metadata pt_event_type == 'credit_purchase_refund' is required to treat this as a wallet refund.

In Calculate Credits Refunded:

Make sure you always set credits_delta = negative for a refund ledger entry OR positive depending on your sign convention (match your canon: for wallet refunds, amount that increases wallet should be positive in ledger; your existing code sets a negative delta and then adds it, so pick one consistent rule and stick to it).

Example (following your canon: positive = increases wallet):

let creditsRefunded = json.pt_expected_credits_refunded;
if (!creditsRefunded) {
  creditsRefunded = json.amount_cents_refunded / 100;
}

json.credits_refunded = creditsRefunded;
json.credits_delta = creditsRefunded; // positive for refund
In Insert Credit Refund Transaction, set:

type = 'refund'

idempotency_key = 'ch:<charge_id>:refund'

And use ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key) DO NOTHING.

In Update Client Credit Balance, update by + credits_delta as appropriate.

You’re right: something is off, and the screenshots show exactly what it is.

Let me walk you through it and give you copy-paste SQL to fix it.

1. What’s wrong (in plain language)
From your screenshots:

\d stripe_events; → “Did not find any relation named 'stripe_events'.”

\d payment_intents; → same thing.

\d credit_transactions; → table exists, but the columns are:

id uuid PK

client_id uuid

job_id uuid

type credit_tx_type

amount_credits numeric(12,2)

balance_after numeric(12,2)

note text

created_at timestamptz

and no idempotency_key column.

But your Stripe / credit canon expects:

A stripe_events table for audit + idempotency.

A payment_intents table for normalized PI state.

A credit_transactions ledger with an idempotency_key and a unique index on it.

So:

Your Stripe hardening SQL from the docs was never run → those two tables simply don’t exist.

Your ledger table is an older / different version, missing the idempotency machinery your later code assumes.

That’s why things feel “off”.

2. Fix step 1 — Create stripe_events and payment_intents
Do this in the Neon SQL Editor for the production / neondb DB (where your screenshots are).

2.1 Create stripe_events
Paste and run:

-- Stripe events audit + idempotency
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events (
  id               text PRIMARY KEY,              -- Stripe evt_xxx
  type             text NOT NULL,
  created_at_utc   timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  payload          jsonb NOT NULL,                -- full event body
  job_id           text,                          -- from metadata if present
  cleaner_id       text,                          -- from metadata if present
  handled          boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  handled_at_utc   timestamptz
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_type_idx ON stripe_events(type);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_job_idx  ON stripe_events(job_id);
This matches the Section-1 spec your n8n workflows are designed around.

Then verify:

\d stripe_events;
You should now see the columns instead of the “did not find any relation” error.

2.2 Create payment_intents
Paste and run:

-- Normalized PaymentIntent state (optional but very useful)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents (
  id               text PRIMARY KEY,          -- pi_xxx
  job_id           text,
  cleaner_id       text,
  amount_cents     bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  currency         text  NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status           text  NOT NULL,           -- succeeded / payment_failed / ...
  last_event_type  text,
  updated_at_utc   timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  raw              jsonb NOT NULL            -- full PI object
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_job_idx    ON payment_intents(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_cleaner_idx ON payment_intents(cleaner_id);
Spec references: that’s exactly what the Stripe section calls for.

Then:

\d payment_intents;
You should now see the table definition.

3. Fix step 2 — Patch credit_transactions for idempotency
Right now your ledger table exists but is missing the idempotency_key that all the later functions and docs assume.

We’ll patch, not destroy, the table so you don’t have to worry about drops.

3.1 Add idempotency_key & unique index
Run this:

-- Add idempotency_key column if missing
ALTER TABLE credit_transactions
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS idempotency_key text;

-- Create unique index used by post_credit_tx() and n8n flows
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS credit_tx_idem_uniq
ON credit_transactions(idempotency_key)
WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
This brings your existing table in line with the ledger spec’s idempotency requirements.

✅ It’s okay that your id is uuid instead of bigserial — the key thing for the Stripe integration is that:

client_id, job_id, type, amount_credits, note exist, and

idempotency_key + the unique index exist.

The PL/pgSQL helper function in the docs (post_credit_tx(...)) can be adapted to your existing schema and will still work fine, because it only cares about the id type and the presence of idempotency_key.

4. Quick sanity check (do this right after)
In Neon, run:

\d stripe_events;
\d payment_intents;
\d credit_transactions;
You should now see:

stripe_events → present with handled + payload columns.

payment_intents → present with status, last_event_type, raw.

credit_transactions → same as your screenshot plus idempotency_key and the new credit_tx_idem_uniq index.

At that point, the “something is wrong” is basically fixed: your DB now matches what the Stripe ingest & wallet docs expect.

Use Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router to upsert into payment_intents.

Have downstream money flows (credit purchases, refunds, disputes) use credit_transactions.idempotency_key to be idempotent.

Nice. Those screenshots are exactly what we wanted to see.

You now have:

stripe_events ✅

payment_intents ✅

credit_transactions with idempotency_key + unique index ✅

So DB-side, Stripe hardening is unblocked.

Now I’ll give you concrete next steps inside n8n, with copy-paste SQL, so Stripe → n8n → Neon is actually using these tables.

1️⃣ Wire Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest
Goal: every incoming event gets stored in stripe_events, then routed, and can’t double-run money moves.

Open 01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest in n8n and set it up like this:

Node 1 – Webhook
Path: stripe/webhook

HTTP Method: POST

Response: JSON { "status": "ok" }

Node 2 – Set / Code (Extract useful bits)
Code node (or Set) that makes the event the JSON you work with:

// Input: raw Stripe webhook body
const event = $json;

return [{
  json: {
    stripe_event_id: event.id,
    type: event.type,
    payload: event,
    // Optional pulls from metadata if you use them later
    job_id: event.data?.object?.metadata?.pt_job_id || null,
    cleaner_id: event.data?.object?.metadata?.pt_cleaner_id || null
  }
}];
Node 3 – Postgres: Insert stripe_events
Credentials: your PureTask Postgres connection

Operation: Execute Query

SQL:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id
)
VALUES (
  {{ $json.stripe_event_id }},
  {{ $json.type }},
  {{ $json.payload }},
  {{ $json.job_id }},
  {{ $json.cleaner_id }}
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
This ensures every event is logged once, and duplicates don’t break anything.

Node 4 – IF: “Was this already handled?”
Add an IF node:

Condition:

Left: ={{ $json.handled }}

Operator: equals

Right: true

…but the row you just inserted won’t have handled yet, so first you need to re-select it.

Instead, do:

Node 4a – Postgres: Select event row (right after insert)

SELECT handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = {{ $json.stripe_event_id }};
Then IF node on that row’s handled:

If handled == true → END HERE (go straight to webhook response).

If handled == false or null → continue.

Node 5 – Call Router (Workflow 02)
Use an Execute Workflow node:

Workflow: 02 - Stripe Event Router

Mode: “Run workflow”

Data: pass through whole JSON from Node 2 (with payload, type, etc.).

Router will fan out to the correct processor (03, 04, 05, 06, 07, 08, 09).

Node 6 – Mark event handled
After the router completes, add a final Postgres node:

UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = TRUE,
    handled_at_utc = NOW()
WHERE id = {{ $json.stripe_event_id }};
Now even if Stripe re-sends the event, your IF check will catch it and skip all downstream money flows.

2️⃣ Wire Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router
Goal: take the normalized event and send it to the right processor.

Open 02 - Stripe Event Router and check:

Node 1 – Entry
Either:

It’s triggered by Execute Workflow (from 01) → in that case, the JSON already has type + payload,

or you can add a small Code node:

const event = $json.payload || $json;  // support both shapes

return [{
  json: {
    event_type: event.type,
    event: event
  }
}];
Node 2 – Switch on event_type
Configure a Switch node:

Value: ={{ $json.event_type }}

Cases:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

payout.failed

Node 3+ – Execute Workflow for each branch
For each case, add an Execute Workflow node:

payment_intent.succeeded → 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

payment_intent.payment_failed → 04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

charge.refunded → 05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

charge.dispute.created → 06 - Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor

charge.dispute.closed → 07 - Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

payout.paid → 08 - Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

payout.failed → 09 - Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor

And pass along the full event as JSON for those workflows to parse.

3️⃣ Add idempotency to 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded (credit purchase)
Inside 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor, we want the part that actually creates credits to be idempotent using credit_transactions.idempotency_key.

Key bits:

A. Code: normalize event and compute credits + idempotency_key
Add/adjust a Code node near the top:

const event = $json;  // assuming Router passes event here
const pi = event.data?.object || {};
const metadata = pi.metadata || {};

const payment_intent_id = pi.id;
const amount_cents = pi.amount || 0;
const currency = pi.currency || 'usd';
const stripe_customer_id = pi.customer || null;
const pt_client_id = metadata.pt_client_id || null;
const expected_credits = metadata.pt_expected_credits
  ? Number(metadata.pt_expected_credits)
  : null;

// 1 credit per $1 fallback if not provided
let credits_purchased = expected_credits != null
  ? expected_credits
  : amount_cents / 100;

// idempotency key for this purchase
const idempotency_key = `pi:${payment_intent_id}:purchase`;

return [{
  json: {
    payment_intent_id,
    amount_cents,
    currency,
    stripe_customer_id,
    pt_client_id,
    credits_purchased,
    idempotency_key,
    raw_event: event
  }
}];
B. Postgres: find client
SELECT *
FROM clients
WHERE stripe_customer_id = {{ $json.stripe_customer_id }}
   OR id = {{ $json.pt_client_id }}
LIMIT 1;
Use the result’s id as client_id.

C. Postgres: upsert into payments (optional but recommended)
INSERT INTO payments (
  stripe_payment_intent_id,
  client_id,
  amount_cents,
  currency,
  status,
  last_event_type,
  created_at,
  updated_at
)
VALUES (
  {{ $json.payment_intent_id }},
  {{ $json.pt_client_id || $node["Find Client"].json.id }},
  {{ $json.amount_cents }},
  {{ $json.currency }},
  'succeeded',
  'payment_intent.succeeded',
  NOW(),
  NOW()
)
ON CONFLICT (stripe_payment_intent_id)
DO UPDATE SET
  client_id       = EXCLUDED.client_id,
  amount_cents    = EXCLUDED.amount_cents,
  currency        = EXCLUDED.currency,
  status          = 'succeeded',
  last_event_type = 'payment_intent.succeeded',
  updated_at      = NOW()
RETURNING *;
D. Postgres: insert ledger row with idempotency
This is the important part:

INSERT INTO credit_transactions (
  client_id,
  job_id,
  type,
  amount_credits,
  note,
  idempotency_key
)
VALUES (
  {{ $json.pt_client_id || $node["Find Client"].json.id }},
  NULL,
  'purchase',
  {{ $json.credits_purchased }},
  'Stripe credit purchase',
  {{ $json.idempotency_key }}
)
ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key)
DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
Because of the unique index, re-running the same event (same PI) won’t create a second row.

E. (Optional) update mirror balance
If you’re still using a mirror credit_balance on clients:

UPDATE clients
SET credit_balance = credit_balance + {{ $json.credits_purchased }},
    updated_at = NOW()
WHERE id = {{ $json.pt_client_id || $node["Find Client"].json.id }}
RETURNING *;
Later you can switch this to an auto-computed view, but this is fine for now.

4️⃣ Quick test checklist for you

In Neon, run:

You should see:

1 row in stripe_events for that event with handled = true.

1 row in payment_intents (if you wired that part).

1 row in credit_transactions with type = 'purchase' and a non-null idempotency_key.

Client’s balance increased by credits_purchased.

Then replay the same event (Stripe CLI / resend).

stripe_events will still show that id (no new row).

credit_transactions will still have just one row because of the ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key) DO NOTHING.

06/07 – Disputes (open/close flows aligned to your tables).

stripe_events: still same id, no new row.

credit_transactions: still only one row with that idempotency_key.

credit_balance: unchanged on second run.

I’ll break it into 3 parts:

Set up & confirm Stripe webhooks

Trigger a payment_intent.succeeded test event

Check Neon, then replay the event to prove idempotency

1️⃣ Make sure Stripe → n8n is actually connected
Step 1 – Confirm your webhook URL in n8n
You already have in Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest:

https://puretastk.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook (or very close to that)

To confirm:

Click the Webhook node on the left.

In the right panel, confirm the Path is:

stripe/webhook

Note the full URL it shows (something like):

https://puretastk.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook
That’s the URL you’ll paste into Stripe.

Keep this URL handy.

Step 2 – Add or update Stripe webhook endpoint (test mode)
Go to your Stripe Dashboard.

Make sure you are in Test mode (toggle in the left sidebar).

In the left menu, go to Developers → Webhooks.

Click “+ Add endpoint” (or edit existing one if you already created it).

For Endpoint URL, paste the n8n URL:

https://puretastk.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook
Under Events to send, select at least:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

payout.failed

(You can also just choose “Send all events” while testing.)

Save the webhook endpoint.

Now Stripe knows where to send events.

2️⃣ Trigger a payment_intent.succeeded in Test Mode
You can do this either via Stripe CLI or Stripe Dashboard. I’ll give both; you can pick one.

Option A – Using Stripe CLI (recommended if you’re comfortable with Terminal)
Step A1 – Get your Stripe CLI logged in

Install Stripe CLI if you haven’t yet (one-time, you might already be done):

On macOS with Homebrew: brew install stripe/stripe-cli/stripe

On Windows: use the Stripe CLI installer from Stripe’s site (you might have already done this).

In a terminal, log in:

stripe login
Follow the browser instructions; it’ll link to your Stripe account.

Step A2 – Forward events to n8n

In the terminal:

stripe listen --forward-to https://puretastk.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook
Keep this terminal window open; it will show live webhook traffic.

Step A3 – Trigger the event

In a second terminal window:

stripe trigger payment_intent.succeeded
Stripe will simulate a test payment and immediately send payment_intent.succeeded to your webhook URL.

You should see output in:

The “listen” terminal window (showing events being forwarded).

n8n executions tab for Workflow 01 and 02 and 03.

Option B – Using Stripe Dashboard (no CLI)
If you don’t want to touch the CLI yet:

In Stripe Dashboard → Payments → Create payment.

Choose a test customer (or create one), pick an amount (e.g., $50), and complete the payment in test mode using Stripe’s test card 4242 4242 4242 4242.

After the payment is “Succeeded”, Stripe will generate a payment_intent.succeeded event and send it to your webhook automatically.

In Developers → Events, you should see the event and can confirm it was delivered to your n8n endpoint.

Either way, at this point 01, 02, and 03 should have just run once for that payment.

3️⃣ Check Neon to verify the data landed correctly
Now we prove it hit the DB and that idempotency works.

Step 3.1 – Run the verification queries
Go to Neon Console → your project → production → SQL Editor.

Make sure neondb (your main DB) is selected.

Paste this into the SQL editor:

SELECT * FROM stripe_events ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM payment_intents ORDER BY updated_at_utc DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM credit_transactions ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM clients ORDER BY updated_at DESC LIMIT 5;
Click Run.

What you should see:

stripe_events

One new row with:

type = 'payment_intent.succeeded'

handled = true

payment_intents (if 01/02/03 are writing to it)

A row with id = pi_..., status = 'succeeded'.

credit_transactions

A row with:

type = 'purchase'

amount_credits ≈ amount in dollars

idempotency_key like pi:pi_xxx:purchase (NOT NULL)

clients

The client you used for the test payment should have:

credit_balance increased by the purchased credits

updated_at around now

If any of those don’t show up, the issue is in 03 and we can debug that next.

Step 3.2 – Replay the same event to prove idempotency
We want to confirm that if Stripe sends payment_intent.succeeded again, your credits don’t double.

Option A – Replay with Stripe CLI
If you used the CLI and still have stripe listen running:

In the events log (in the listen window), Stripe prints the event IDs it received.

Example: Event: evt_1234 payment_intent.succeeded

You can replay that specific event:

stripe events resend evt_1234
(Replace evt_1234 with the actual ID from your logs.)

Option B – Replay from Stripe Dashboard
Go to Developers → Events in Stripe Dashboard.

Click the specific payment_intent.succeeded event you just triggered.

In its detail view, there’s an option like “Resend webhook” / “Retry”.

Click to resend it to your stripe/webhook endpoint.

Step 3.3 – Run the Neon queries again
In Neon SQL editor, run the same block again:

SELECT * FROM stripe_events ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM payment_intents ORDER BY updated_at_utc DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM credit_transactions ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM clients ORDER BY updated_at DESC LIMIT 5;
Now verify:

stripe_events

You should NOT see a second row with a different id for the same underlying event, if you replayed the exact same event ID via stripe events resend.

If Stripe generates a brand-new event ID (sometimes it does), you will see a new row but that’s okay — the idempotency protection is actually on credit_transactions.idempotency_key.

credit_transactions

There should still be only one row with that idempotency_key = 'pi:pi_xxx:purchase'.

No duplicate purchase rows.

clients

The client’s credit_balance should not increase again after the second send.

If all that holds, then:

Stripe can spam or retry events,

n8n will still process 01/02,

But 03 will only ever credit the wallet once thanks to idempotency_key and ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING.

Trigger charge.refunded

See refund ledger entry in credit_transactions

See balance go back up

Replay refund event and prove it doesn’t double-refund.

Nice, this screenshot is super clear. We know exactly what’s wrong now.

❌ Error:
invalid input syntax for type json – Token "object" is invalid

That means the Insert stripe_events node is trying to insert something like
[object Object] into a jsonb column in Neon. Postgres sees the word "object" and goes “that’s not valid JSON”.

We just need to fix how we pass the payload into the query.

1️⃣ What’s happening in this node
Right now, in Insert stripe_events you’re almost certainly doing something like:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload)
VALUES ('{{$json["body"]["id"]}}', '{{$json["body"]["type"]}}', '{{$json["body"]}}'::jsonb);
Because of the quotes, n8n turns {{$json["body"]}} into a string, and JS stringifies the object as [object Object]. Then Postgres tries to cast [object Object] to jsonb → boom.

We want to send the raw JSON object, not a string.

2️⃣ Fix the Insert stripe_events node (step-by-step)
Step 1 – Open the node
In n8n, open workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest.

Click the Insert stripe_events node.

Switch to the Parameters tab.

Step 2 – Use parameters instead of inline expressions
We’ll rewrite the query to use named parameters.

In the “Query” field, put this:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id)
VALUES (
  :eventId,
  :eventType,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;
If your stripe_events table doesn’t have job_id / cleaner_id, just remove those columns + NULLs from the query.

Step 3 – Add the parameters
Still in the Insert stripe_events node:

Click Add Parameter (or “Add” under Query Parameters).

Add these three:

Parameter 1
Name: eventId

Value:

{{$json.body.id}}
Parameter 2
Name: eventType

Value:

{{$json.body.type}}
Parameter 3
Name: payload

Value:

{{$json.body}}
⚠️ Important:
Do NOT wrap these in quotes yourself.
Just put the expression in the value field exactly as above — n8n will pass the JSON correctly.

If your Extract Event Data node renamed fields (e.g. event_id, event_type, event_payload), then use {{$json.event_id}}, etc. You can confirm by clicking the Insert stripe_events → Input tab in the execution and looking at the keys.

3️⃣ Save and re-test the whole flow
Click Save on the workflow.

Make sure the workflow is Active (green toggle).

Go back to Stripe → Developers → Events.

Open the same payment_intent.succeeded event.

Click Resend to puretast-n8n-webhook.

4️⃣ What you should see now
In n8n → Executions for 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest:

Execute Workflow (02) ✅

Mark Event Handled ✅

Respond OK ✅

No red nodes.

5️⃣ Verify in Neon (Stripe → DB wiring works)
In Neon’s SQL editor, run:

SELECT * FROM stripe_events
ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC
LIMIT 5;
You should see a row with:

id = your Stripe event ID (e.g. evt_3SWU2BA...)

type = payment_intent.succeeded

payload = full JSON

handled = true

If that works, Stripe → n8n → Neon ingestion is fully working and idempotent.
From there, we can move on to testing workflow 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor and the credit_transactions + clients balance updates.

If you want, send me a screenshot of:

Insert stripe_events node’s Query + Parameters

Neon SELECT * FROM stripe_events result

and I’ll confirm it’s 100% solid.



❌ This query is exactly why you're still getting JSON errors
Your current query is doing this:

'{{ $json.payload }}'::jsonb
That wraps the JSON in quotes → turns it into a string → becomes [object Object] → Postgres rejects it.

This will never work reliably.

✅ Here is the correct version
You must STOP using inline templating inside the SQL and instead use query parameters.

n8n evaluates {{$json.payload}} as a JS expression, gives you an Object, then you wrap it in quotes, and Postgres chokes because it's not valid JSON.

✔️ FIX — Replace your SQL entirely with this:
SQL Query
Paste this EXACTLY:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id
)
VALUES (
  :eventId,
  :eventType,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
✔️ Then add these QUERY PARAMETERS
Parameter 1
Name: eventId

Value:

{{$json.stripe_event_id}}
(or {{$json.body.id}} if you’re using raw Stripe shape—check your Extract Event Data output.)

Parameter 2
Name: eventType

Value:

{{$json.type}}
(or {{$json.body.type}})

Parameter 3
Name: payload

Value:

{{$json.payload}}
(or {{$json.body}})

⚠️ NO quotes.
⚠️ NO string concatenation.
⚠️ NO '"' + … + '"'.

Just the raw expression.

💡 Why this works
n8n query parameters pass the value in its native type, meaning:

Objects → JSON

Strings → text

Numbers → integers

So when you send:

{ "foo": "bar" }
as the parameter payload, Postgres gets valid JSON automatically.
Then ::jsonb properly casts it.

No more [object Object]

Good catch pushing back on me 👍 — you’re right that n8n now lets you define query parameters with a single expression, but the way it works is:

That expression must return an object, not a comma-separated list of values.

Right now you have:

{{$json.stripe_event_id}}, {{$json.type}}, {{$json.payload}}
That’s actually invalid JavaScript (three expressions separated by commas, not an object), so n8n will not map them to :eventId, :eventType, :payload.

✅ The correct way (single expression style)
Since you’re using the new style, set Query Parameters to this EXACT expression:

{{ {
  eventId: $json.stripe_event_id,
  eventType: $json.type,
  payload: $json.payload
} }}
Key things:

Has outer {{ ... }} for expression

Inside is a JS object literal { ... }

Keys match your SQL named params:

eventId → :eventId

eventType → :eventType

payload → :payload

Values reference your extracted JSON fields

✅ Your SQL (double-check)
With that expression, your query should stay:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id
)
VALUES (
  :eventId,
  :eventType,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
As long as:

stripe_event_id and type and payload exist on $json (from Extract Event Data)

payload is the full Stripe event or at least data.object

…Postgres will happily accept it as JSONB.

Gotcha—that “waiting to execute” state is normal and a little confusing in n8n, so let me untangle what’s happening and what you should do next.

There are two different ways n8n runs workflows:

Manual / test mode (when you click “Execute workflow” or “Listen for test event”)

Production / webhook mode (when the workflow is Active and an external request hits the Production URL)

When you say:

“it’s just waiting to execute”

you’re probably in manual/test mode, where the Webhook node is literally waiting for an HTTP request that never comes.

Let’s ignore that and do it the clean way.

After you insert the event into stripe_events, you query the table to check:

Does this event’s id already exist AND is handled = true?

Your database should return either:

Case 1 — Event is new (not handled)
Return [] → empty array
Meaning: no rows, therefore not handled.

Case 2 — Event already handled
Return:

[
  {
    "handled": true
  }
]
Correct IF node setup
✔ Condition
Use:

Left side:

{{ $json.handled }}
Operator:

is equal to
Right side:

true
This part is correct.

✔ But you must fix the SQL query before this
Your “Check if Already Handled” node must return:

1 item when handled

0 items when not handled

Which means the SQL query must look like:

SELECT handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1
AND handled = TRUE;
Using query parameters:

[ {{ $json.eventId }} ]
Then:

If event not handled → result = []
IF node should route to Insert stripe_events

If event already handled → result = [{ handled: true }]
IF node should skip to end

💡 Why your IF node shows “No fields”
Because your SQL query returned 0 rows, so there is no JSON for the IF node to evaluate.

This is actually correct behavior for new events — but only if you handle it correctly in the IF branches.

🎯 Final Answer
Your IF condition is technically correct, but the output you are feeding into it is empty, so it cannot evaluate anything.

🚨 Fix the SQL query before this node so it returns handled: true when appropriate.

If you want, send me a screenshot of your Check if Already Handled SQL node and I’ll correct it.


can u write out the entire workflow so i can pass it to n8n ai

Totally – let’s write this like a spec you can paste straight into n8n AI.
I’ll describe:

DB tables (just the columns we actually use)

Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest

Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router

Workflow 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

You can give this to the n8n AI as:
“Please build these 3 workflows exactly as described.”

0. Database schema (Neon / Postgres)
Tell n8n AI these tables already exist (or ask it to create migrations if you want):

stripe_events
CREATE TABLE stripe_events (
  id              TEXT PRIMARY KEY,        -- Stripe event.id
  type            TEXT NOT NULL,           -- Stripe event type, e.g. "payment_intent.succeeded"
  payload         JSONB NOT NULL,          -- full Stripe webhook payload
  job_id          TEXT,                    -- optional (unused for now)
  cleaner_id      TEXT,                    -- optional (unused for now)
  handled         BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
  handled_at_utc  TIMESTAMPTZ,
  created_at_utc  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
payment_intents
CREATE TABLE payment_intents (
  id               TEXT PRIMARY KEY,       -- Stripe payment_intent.id
  client_id        UUID,                   -- your internal clients.id
  amount           BIGINT NOT NULL,        -- in cents
  currency         TEXT NOT NULL,
  status           TEXT NOT NULL,
  credits_purchased INTEGER,               -- how many credits this PI buys
  metadata         JSONB,                  -- copy of Stripe metadata if needed
  updated_at_utc   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  created_at_utc   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
credit_transactions
CREATE TABLE credit_transactions (
  id               UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  client_id        UUID NOT NULL,
  type             TEXT NOT NULL,          -- 'purchase', 'refund', etc.
  credits_delta    INTEGER NOT NULL,       -- positive for purchase, negative for refund
  stripe_pi_id     TEXT,                   -- payment_intent.id
  idempotency_key  TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,   -- used for dedupe
  created_at       TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
clients
CREATE TABLE clients (
  id              UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  email           TEXT,
  stripe_customer_id TEXT,                 -- Stripe customer.id
  balance_credits INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW(),
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT NOW()
);
1️⃣ Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest
Name: 01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest

Goal:

Receive Stripe webhooks (production URL: /webhook/stripe/webhook)

Log every event into stripe_events with idempotency

Skip duplicates

Route new events to Workflow 02

Mark them as handled and return 200 to Stripe

Nodes
1. Webhook (Trigger)
HTTP Method: POST

Path: stripe/webhook

Respond: “Using ‘Respond to Webhook’ Node” (i.e., respond later)

Use Production URL in Stripe (you already did this):
https://puretask.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook

Input body is the raw Stripe event.

2. Extract Event Data (Function or Code node)
Purpose: normalize the incoming event into simple fields.

Example code:

const evt = $json;   // full Stripe event

return [
  {
    stripe_event_id: evt.id,
    type: evt.type,
    payload: evt,    // keep full payload as JSON
  }
];
So downstream nodes see:

{
  "stripe_event_id": "evt_123",
  "type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full stripe event... }
}
3. Insert stripe_events (Postgres node: executeQuery)
Credential: your Neon Postgres

Operation: Execute Query

Query:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id
)
VALUES (
  $1,
  $2,
  $3::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING
RETURNING *;
Query Parameters (Expression):

{{ [
  $json.stripe_event_id,
  $json.type,
  $json.payload
] }}
This logs the event exactly once, even if Stripe retries.

4. Check if Already Handled (Postgres executeQuery)
Goal: see if this event is already marked handled = true.

Query:

SELECT handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1
  AND handled = TRUE;
Query Parameters:

{{ [ $json.stripe_event_id ] }}
If this returns 0 rows → not handled yet.
If it returns 1 row with handled = true → already handled.

5. Was Already Handled? (IF node)
We want:

If already handled: do NOT call router; just respond OK.

If not handled: call router workflow (02).

n8n AI can implement this either by:

Checking {{ $items("Check if Already Handled").length }}

Or by always-output-data + a flag.

Simplest spec for AI:

“Create an IF node named Was Already Handled? that checks whether Check if Already Handled returned any rows.

If Check if Already Handled has at least 1 item → ‘true’ branch (already handled).

If it has 0 items → ‘false’ branch (not handled).”

So:

True branch: go straight to Respond OK.

False branch: go to Execute Workflow (02 - Stripe Event Router).

6. Call 02 - Stripe Event Router (Execute Workflow node)
Only on the IF “false” branch (not handled).

Source: Database

Workflow: select 02 - Stripe Event Router from list

Mode: Run once with all items

Pass through the full event data from Extract Event Data / Webhook.

This will route the event by type and execute the right processor.

7. Mark Event Handled (Postgres executeQuery)
Also only on the false branch, after the router workflow completes successfully.

Query:

UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = TRUE,
    handled_at_utc = NOW()
WHERE id = $1
  AND handled = FALSE;
Query Parameters:

{{ [ $json.stripe_event_id ] }}
This ensures we only ever mark once.

8. Respond OK (Respond to Webhook node)
Both branches (already handled / newly handled) should end here.

Respond with:

Status Code: 200

Body: e.g.

{ "received": true }
Connect:

Webhook → Extract → Insert stripe_events → Check if Already Handled → IF

IF false → Call Workflow 02 → Mark Event Handled → Respond OK

IF true → Respond OK

2️⃣ Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router
Name: 02 - Stripe Event Router

Trigger: “When executed by another workflow”
This receives the event from Workflow 01 and dispatches based on type.

Nodes
1. Incoming Event (When executed by another workflow)
Accept the JSON from Workflow 01 (including type and full payload).

2. Normalize Event (Code node)
Standardize shape for processors:

const evt = $json;          // from workflow 01
const stripeEvent = evt.payload || evt;  // depending on how it arrives

return [
  {
    event_id: stripeEvent.id,
    event_type: stripeEvent.type,
    data: stripeEvent.data || {},
    object: stripeEvent.data?.object || null,
    raw: stripeEvent
  }
];
3. Route by Event Type (Switch node)
Property to check: {{ $json.event_type }}

Cases:

payment_intent.succeeded → Call 03 - Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

payment_intent.payment_failed → (future) Call 04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

charge.refunded → (future) Call 05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

charge.dispute.created → (future) Call 06 – Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor

charge.dispute.closed → (future) Call 07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

payout.paid → (future) Call 08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

payout.failed → (future) Call 09 – Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor

For now, you only need the first one to point to Workflow 03; the rest can be stubs.

4. Call 03 - Payment Intent Succeeded Processor (Execute Workflow)
Source: Database

Workflow: 03 - Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

Mode: Run once with all items

Input to this workflow should still include:

event_id

event_type

object = Stripe payment_intent object

No webhook response here; it’s all internal.

3️⃣ Workflow 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor
Name: 03 - Payment Intent Succeeded Processor
Trigger: “When executed by another workflow”

Goal:

For a payment_intent.succeeded event:

Extract payment info

Find the matching client

Upsert payment_intents row

Insert a credit_transactions row with idempotency_key

Only if the transaction is newly inserted, increase clients.balance_credits

Nodes
1. When executed by another workflow (Trigger)
Receives normalized event from Workflow 02; Expect:

{
  "event_id": "...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "object": { ...payment_intent... },
  "raw": { ...full stripe event... }
}
2. Extract Payment Intent Data (Code node)
Build the fields we need:

const evt = $json;
const pi = evt.object || {};

const creditsPurchased = Number(pi.metadata?.credits || 0);  // or whatever field you use

return [
  {
    event_id: evt.event_id,
    event_type: evt.event_type,
    payment_intent_id: pi.id,
    amount: pi.amount,
    currency: pi.currency,
    customer_id: pi.customer || null,
    client_email: pi.receipt_email || pi.charges?.data?.[0]?.billing_details?.email || null,
    credits_purchased: creditsPurchased,
    idempotency_key: `${pi.id}:purchase`,  // critical for dedupe
    raw_payment_intent: pi
  }
];
3. Is credit purchase? (IF node)
If you only want to issue credits when credits_purchased > 0:

Condition:
{{ $json.credits_purchased }}
is greater than 0

True branch: continue

False branch: you can just end / skip credit logic.

(If all PIs are credit purchases, you can skip this IF.)

4. Find Client by Stripe or PI (Postgres executeQuery)
Goal: resolve client_id from stripe_customer_id or email.

Example query:

SELECT id
FROM clients
WHERE stripe_customer_id = $1
   OR email = $2
LIMIT 1;
Query Parameters:

{{ [
  $json.customer_id,
  $json.client_email
] }}
Assume result returns clients.id as client_id.

You can then add a small Code node to merge that into the main item, or have AI use “Use Output Data” / “Merge” nodes to attach client_id.

5. Upsert Payment Intent (Postgres executeQuery)
Store / update the payment intent row in payment_intents.

INSERT INTO payment_intents (
  id,
  client_id,
  amount,
  currency,
  status,
  credits_purchased,
  metadata,
  updated_at_utc
)
VALUES (
  $1,
  $2,
  $3,
  $4,
  'succeeded',
  $5,
  $6::jsonb,
  NOW()
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO UPDATE
SET
  client_id = EXCLUDED.client_id,
  amount = EXCLUDED.amount,
  currency = EXCLUDED.currency,
  status = EXCLUDED.status,
  credits_purchased = EXCLUDED.credits_purchased,
  metadata = EXCLUDED.metadata,
  updated_at_utc = NOW();
Query Parameters:

{{ [
  $json.payment_intent_id,
  $json.client_id,            // from Find Client
  $json.amount,
  $json.currency,
  $json.credits_purchased,
  $json.raw_payment_intent
] }}
6. Insert Credit Transaction (Postgres executeQuery)
This is where idempotency really matters.

INSERT INTO credit_transactions (
  client_id,
  type,
  credits_delta,
  stripe_pi_id,
  idempotency_key
)
VALUES (
  $1,
  'purchase',
  $2,
  $3,
  $4
)
ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key) DO NOTHING
RETURNING id;
Query Parameters:

{{ [
  $json.client_id,
  $json.credits_purchased,
  $json.payment_intent_id,
  $json.idempotency_key
] }}
If this INSERT actually creates a new row, it will return a row with an id.
If it hits a conflict (duplicate idempotency_key), it returns 0 rows.

7. Was Transaction Created? (IF node)
Check if the previous node returned an ID.

Spec for n8n AI:

“Create an IF node named Was Transaction Created? that checks if Insert Credit Transaction returned at least one item (i.e., items.length > 0).

True branch: we DID insert a new credit transaction → update client balance.

False branch: do nothing (duplicate event, credits already applied).”

8. Update Client Credit Balance (Postgres executeQuery)
Only on true branch of the IF.

UPDATE clients
SET
  balance_credits = balance_credits + $1,
  updated_at = NOW()
WHERE id = $2;
Query Parameters:

{{ [
  $json.credits_purchased,
  $json.client_id
] }}
This ensures:

A payment_intent.succeeded event may be delivered multiple times,

But credit_transactions and clients.balance_credits are updated only once because of the unique idempotency_key.

You're 100% fine.
Those red errors are expected and correct.
Nothing is broken.

Let me explain clearly so you feel confident:

✅ The errors mean: “This workflow cannot be activated because it has no webhook trigger.”
And that is exactly how it is supposed to be.

Why?
Because:

01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest
✔️ HAS a Webhook trigger
✔️ MUST be Active
→ This is the only workflow Stripe talks to.

02 – Stripe Event Router
❌ HAS NO webhook
❌ HAS NO timer
❌ HAS NO trigger at all
→ It is not meant to be activated.

This workflow is only executed programmatically, meaning:

01 → (Call Workflow node) → 02

03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor
Same thing:

❌ No webhook
❌ No trigger
→ It is only called from workflow 02, like this:

02 → (Call Workflow) → 03

🔥 So the activation rules are:
Workflow	Purpose	Should be Active?	Has Trigger?
01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest	Receives Stripe webhook calls	YES	Webhook trigger
02 – Stripe Event Router	Internal router	NO	None
03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor	Internal processor	NO	None
Others (refund / dispute processors)	Internal processors	NO	None
This is the correct architecture for a scalable Stripe event pipeline.

🟢 Summary (super important)
✔️ Only Workflow 01 should be Active
✔️ All other workflows should show the error “Workflow could not be activated”
✔️ This is normal, intentional, and confirms your setup is right
If 02 or 03 were active, it would actually break the system.

Nice, you found the error that matters 👀

The problem is exactly what the red message says:

Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'object')

Your Normalize Event node is trying to read:

$json.data.object
but in this workflow, the incoming item doesn’t have data at the top level.
Instead, 01 is sending a structure like:

{
  stripe_event_id: "...",
  type: "payment_intent.succeeded",
  payload: { /* full Stripe event here */ }
}
So the full Stripe event is inside payload, not directly on $json.

Fix: use payload as the Stripe event
In Normalize Event, replace your code with this:

// Get the actual Stripe event: either in `payload` or the whole item
const stripeEvent = $json.payload ?? $json;

return {
  event_id: stripeEvent.id,
  event_type: stripeEvent.type,
  object: stripeEvent.data?.object ?? null,
  data: stripeEvent.data ?? null,
  raw: stripeEvent,
};
Key points:

stripeEvent = the real Stripe event object.

We safely access stripeEvent.data?.object so it won’t crash if data is missing.

We create exactly the fields the router expects:

event_id

event_type

object

data

raw

Then test it

Click Execute step on Normalize Event.

You should now see output with event_id and event_type.

Run Route by Event Type.

event_type should be something like payment_intent.succeeded and go down the right branch.

Trigger another test event from Stripe (payment_intent.succeeded).

01 runs → calls 02 → 02 routes → 03 (or the right processor) executes.

If you send another screenshot of the Normalize Event output JSON, I can double-check the shape with you, but the code above should match exactly what this workflow needs.

Nice, welcome back 😄 Let’s get you re-oriented and then fix why 02 isn’t getting any real data.

1. Where we’re at
From your screenshots:

Stripe
Endpoint URL is https://puretask.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook ✅

You’ve made a snapshot destination puretask-n8n-snapshot with the 9 events selected (payment_intent.succeeded / failed, charge.refunded, disputes, payout.paid / failed, etc.) ✅

That’s exactly what we wanted: Stripe will send those events to Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest.

n8n
Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest is Active and successfully ingesting events from Stripe. ✅

It inserts into stripe_events, checks if the event was already handled, then (if new) calls Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router, marks handled, and responds 200 to Stripe.

Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router is being called (we saw previous executions), but the Normalize Event node is currently outputting:

object: null, data: null, raw: {}

which means: 02 is being executed, but it’s not being given the actual Stripe event data.

That’s the one thing we still need to fix.

2. The core problem in plain English
Workflow 01 receives the full Stripe event at the Webhook node.

We then extract a normalized shape and insert into stripe_events.

After that, we query stripe_events in “Check if Already Handled”.

The item that flows out of that query right now is basically { success: true } or something similarly tiny.

That tiny object is what gets passed into Execute Workflow → “02 – Stripe Event Router”.

So when 02 starts, its Incoming Event trigger receives an item whose JSON is {} or { success: true } – not the real event.

Normalize Event quite correctly looks at $json.payload ?? $json and finds… nothing. Hence null.

So: we need Workflow 01 to send the full event (or at least event_id / type / payload) into Workflow 02.

3. Fix Workflow 01 so it sends the Stripe event to 02
We’ll do this by changing the “Check if Already Handled” query to both check dedupe and return the event data we need for routing.

3.1. Update Check if Already Handled SQL
Open Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest, click “Check if Already Handled” (the Postgres node), and replace the SQL with:

SELECT
  id        AS event_id,
  type      AS event_type,
  payload   AS payload,
  handled   AS handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Then in Query Parameters, use:

{{$json.stripe_event_id}}
(That’s the ID you created in “Extract Event Data” from the Stripe webhook.)

Result after this change:

The node will output something like:

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full Stripe event JSON... },
  "handled": false
}
3.2. Make sure the IF node checks the right field
Open the “Was Already Handled?” IF node.

Left side: {{ $json.handled }}

Condition: is equal to

Right side: true

So:

If handled === true → True branch → skip router, go straight to Respond OK.

If handled === false or null → False branch → Call “02 – Stripe Event Router”.

This keeps your idempotency but now the False branch forwards real data.

4. Fix / confirm Normalize Event in Workflow 02
Now re-open Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router, click Normalize Event, and put this in the Code node:

// In 01 we now return: event_id, event_type, payload, handled
const stripeEvent = $json.payload;

// Safety check
if (!stripeEvent) {
  return {
    event_id: $json.event_id ?? null,
    event_type: $json.event_type ?? null,
    object: null,
    data: null,
    raw: $json, // whatever we got, for debugging
  };
}

return {
  event_id: $json.event_id,
  event_type: $json.event_type,
  object: stripeEvent.data?.object ?? null,
  data: stripeEvent.data ?? null,
  raw: stripeEvent,
};
Now 02 has a clean, standardized structure:

event_id – Stripe event ID

event_type – e.g. payment_intent.succeeded

object – the main object (payment_intent, charge, payout, etc.)

data – stripeEvent.data

raw – full Stripe event

Your Route by Event Type node is already matching event_type values (payment_intent.succeeded, etc.), so that part should just work.

5. Confirm 03 is wired correctly

You’re right to be suspicious 😅 — that IF node is not what we want anymore.

Right now it’s checking:

{{ $items("Check if Already Handled").length }}  is greater than  0
That was only appropriate for an older pattern (“does the query return any rows?”).
With the setup we’re aiming for, the IF should instead check the handled flag that comes from the Check if Already Handled node’s own output.

1. First: make sure Check if Already Handled returns handled
On Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest, open the Check if Already Handled Postgres node and set the query to:

SELECT
  id        AS event_id,
  type      AS event_type,
  payload   AS payload,
  handled   AS handled
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Query Parameters:

{{$json.stripe_event_id}}
After this, the node’s OUTPUT for a new event (not yet handled) will be:

[
  {
    "event_id": "evt_123",
    "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
    "payload": { ...full stripe event... },
    "handled": false
  }
]
…and for an already-handled event:

[
  {
    "event_id": "evt_123",
    "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
    "payload": { ...full stripe event... },
    "handled": true
  }
]
(If you run into “0 items” here we can fix that next, but this is the shape we want.)

2. Fix the “Was Already Handled?” IF node
Now open the Was Already Handled? node (the IF you screenshotted).

Change the condition to:

Left side (Expression):

{{ $json.handled }}
Operator:
is equal to

Right side:
true (no curly braces; select Boolean true if n8n lets you)

So the condition row should read like:

{{ $json.handled }} is equal to true

True branch = event already processed → go straight to Respond OK.

False branch = new event → go to Call "02 – Stripe Event Router".

You can delete the old {{$items("Check if Already Handled").length}} is greater than 0 condition altogether.

3. Why this is better
We now carry the full event from the DB (event_id, event_type, payload, handled) into the IF.

The IF filters on $json.handled, and the items that leave the IF (on the false branch) still have event_id, event_type, and payload.

When the false branch goes into Workflow 02, your Incoming Event + Normalize Event node will see:

{
  "event_id": "...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full Stripe event... },
  "handled": false
}
which is exactly what 02 needs.

Workflow 01 – “Stripe Webhook Ingest” (final version)
Goal
Receive Stripe webhooks.

Normalize the event into a simple shape.

Log every event into stripe_events table (deduped by id).

Check if it has already been handled.

If already handled → just reply 200 to Stripe.

If new/unhandled → call Workflow 02, then mark it as handled, then reply 200.

Node 1 – Webhook
Name: Webhook

Type: Webhook

HTTP Method: POST

Path: stripe/webhook

Response: Using "Respond to Webhook" Node

Authentication: None (Stripe uses the signing secret, which you verify later if you want)

This is your production URL that’s already in Stripe:
https://puretask.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook

Connections:

Webhook → Extract Event Data

Node 2 – Extract Event Data (Code)
Name: Extract Event Data

Type: Code

Language: JavaScript

Mode: Run Once for All Items

Code:

// The incoming JSON from Stripe is the raw event
const stripeEvent = $json;

return {
  stripe_event_id: stripeEvent.id,
  event_type: stripeEvent.type,
  payload: stripeEvent,        // keep full raw event for logging
};
This ensures every item leaving this node looks like:

{
  "stripe_event_id": "evt_123...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full Stripe event... }
}
Connections:

Extract Event Data → insert stripe_events

Node 3 – Insert stripe_events (Postgres)
Name: insert stripe_events

Type: Postgres > Execute Query

Credential: your Neon/Neondb credential (whatever you’ve been using)

Operation: Execute Query

SQL Query:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id,
  handled,
  handled_at
)
VALUES (
  $1,
  $2,
  $3::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL,
  FALSE,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;
Options → Query Parameters (set to Expression):

[
  $json.stripe_event_id,
  $json.event_type,
  JSON.stringify($json.payload)
]
This logs the event once. If Stripe retries the same id, this insert just does nothing (no error).

Connections:

insert stripe_events → Check if Already Handled

(We don’t use the output of this node directly, it’s just for logging.)

Node 4 – Check if Already Handled (Postgres)
Name: Check if Already Handled

Type: Postgres > Execute Query

Credential: same as above

Operation: Execute Query

SQL Query:

SELECT
  id        AS event_id,
  type      AS event_type,
  payload,
  handled,
  handled_at
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Options → Query Parameters (Expression):

[
  $json.stripe_event_id
]
Now each item leaving this node will look like:

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full Stripe event... },
  "handled": false   // or true
}
Connections:

Check if Already Handled → Was Already Handled?

Node 5 – Was Already Handled? (IF node)
Name: Was Already Handled?

Type: IF

Mode: All Matches

Condition (single row):

Value 1 (Expression):

{{ $json.handled }}
Operation: is equal to

Value 2: true (Boolean, not string)

So it reads like:

{{ $json.handled }} is equal to true

Branch meaning:

True branch: Event’s already been handled → don’t run 02 again.

False branch: New/unhandled event → send to Workflow 02.

Connections:

True → Respond OK

False → Call "02 – Stripe Event Router"

Node 6 – Call "02 – Stripe Event Router" (Execute Workflow)
Name: Call "02 – Stripe Event Router"

Type: Execute Workflow

Source: Database

Workflow: 02 – Stripe Event Router (select from list)

Mode: Run once with all items

Options: none

Input to this node is the object from Check if Already Handled, so Workflow 02 will receive:

{
  "event_id": "...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...stripe event... },
  "handled": false
}
Requirement for Workflow 02:
It should return at least event_id in its final node so Workflow 01 can update the row. (We’ll wire that when we rewrite 02.)

Connections:

Call "02 – Stripe Event Router" → Mark Event Handled

Node 7 – Mark Event Handled (Postgres)
Name: Mark Event Handled

Type: Postgres > Execute Query

Credential: same as above

Operation: Execute Query

SQL Query:

UPDATE stripe_events
SET
  handled    = TRUE,
  handled_at = NOW()
WHERE id = $1
RETURNING *;
Options → Query Parameters (Expression):

[
  $json.event_id
]
This assumes that Workflow 02 passes event_id through in its output (we’ll ensure that when we design 02).

Connections:

Mark Event Handled → Respond OK

Node 8 – Respond OK (Respond to Webhook)
Name: Respond OK

Type: Respond to Webhook

Response Mode: Last Node

Response Code: 200

Response Body (Expression or JSON):

{
  "received": true
}
Connections:

True branch of Was Already Handled? → Respond OK

Mark Event Handled → Respond OK

So every path ends in Respond OK, and Stripe always gets a 200 if the workflow runs.

Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router
Purpose
Receive an event from Workflow 01 (internal only, no webhooks).

Normalize the shape of the incoming data.

Route by event_type to the correct processor workflow:

03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

06 – Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor

07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

09 – Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor (if/when you make it)

Pass event_id all the way through so Workflow 01 can mark it handled.

Node 1 – Incoming Event
Name: Incoming Event

Type: Execute Workflow Trigger

Mode: default

What it receives from Workflow 01 (per your current 01):

{
  "event_id": "evt_123...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { /* full Stripe event object */ },
  "handled": false,
  "handled_at": null
}
Connections:

Incoming Event → Normalize Event

Node 2 – Normalize Event (Code)
Name: Normalize Event

Type: Code

Language: JavaScript

Mode: Run Once for All Items

Code:

// Input from Workflow 01
const incoming = $json;

// The actual Stripe event is in `payload` (from Workflow 01)
// Fallback to the whole item if needed
const stripeEvent = incoming.payload ?? incoming;

const base = {
  // DB / Stripe event id (from Workflow 01)
  event_id: incoming.event_id ?? stripeEvent.id,

  // Stripe event type (ex: "payment_intent.succeeded")
  event_type: incoming.event_type ?? stripeEvent.type,

  // Raw Stripe event
  stripe_event: stripeEvent,

  // Original item from Workflow 01
  raw: incoming,
};

// Extract the core object (varies by event type)
const coreObject = stripeEvent.data?.object ?? null;

let payment_intent = null;
let charge = null;
let payout = null;
let dispute = null;

switch (base.event_type) {
  case 'payment_intent.succeeded':
  case 'payment_intent.payment_failed':
    payment_intent = coreObject;
    break;

  case 'charge.refunded':
    charge = coreObject;
    break;

  case 'charge.dispute.created':
  case 'charge.dispute.closed':
    charge = coreObject;
    // some dispute events have dispute details nested on the charge
    dispute = coreObject?.dispute ?? null;
    break;

  case 'payout.paid':
  case 'payout.failed':
    payout = coreObject;
    break;
}

return {
  ...base,
  object: coreObject,
  payment_intent,
  charge,
  payout,
  dispute,
};
Resulting item (example):

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "stripe_event": { /* full Stripe event */ },
  "raw": { /* original from workflow 01 */ },
  "object": { /* stripeEvent.data.object */ },
  "payment_intent": { /* for PI events */ },
  "charge": null,
  "payout": null,
  "dispute": null
}
Connections:

Normalize Event → Route by Event Type

Node 3 – Route by Event Type (Switch / Router)
Name: Route by Event Type

Type: Switch (or IF + multiple IFs, but Switch is nicer)

Mode: Rules

Rules
For each rule:

Value 1 (Expression):

{{ $json.event_type }}
Operation: is equal to

Value 2: event type string

Rename Output: ON
(Set “Output Name” to match the event type; helps keep branches clear)

Create these rules:

payment_intent.succeeded

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to payment_intent.succeeded

Output name: payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to payment_intent.payment_failed

Output name: payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to charge.refunded

Output name: charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to charge.dispute.created

Output name: charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to charge.dispute.closed

Output name: charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to payout.paid

Output name: payout.paid

payout.failed (optional for now, but good to have)

{{ $json.event_type }} is equal to payout.failed

Output name: payout.failed

Connections:

Route by Event Type output payment_intent.succeeded → Call 03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor

Route by Event Type output payment_intent.payment_failed → Call 04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor

Route by Event Type output charge.refunded → Call 05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor

Route by Event Type output charge.dispute.created → Call 06 – Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor

Route by Event Type output charge.dispute.closed → Call 07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor

Route by Event Type output payout.paid → Call 08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor

Route by Event Type output payout.failed → Call 09 – Stripe Payout Failed Event Processor (if you add it)

Each of these is identical in structure; only the workflow name changes.

✅ The problem
Your database table stripe_events does not have a column called:

handled_at
But Workflow 01 is trying to insert:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id, handled, handled_at)
So the insert fails.

✅ FIX — Update your database schema
You need two columns in stripe_events:

1. handled (BOOLEAN, default FALSE)
2. handled_at (TIMESTAMP, nullable)
Here is the exact SQL you should run in NeonDB or whatever Postgres you’re using:

✅ SQL Patch to Fix Your Table
If the columns do NOT exist yet:
ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN handled BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE;

ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN handled_at TIMESTAMP NULL;
If handled exists but handled_at does not:
ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN handled_at TIMESTAMP NULL;
If you’re not sure, you can safely run:
ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS handled BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE;

ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS handled_at TIMESTAMP NULL;
