0. What PureTask Actually Needs
For PureTask credits to work correctly you need:

Every Stripe webhook event logged once in stripe_events with idempotency.

Only new / unhandled events routed to processors.

payment_intent.succeeded → credit purchase recorded → client credits increased.

payment_intent.payment_failed / charge.refunded / charge.dispute.* / payout.* → handled by dedicated processors (03–08).

Workflows must be safe to re-send from Stripe (retries, manual “Resend”) without double-processing.

Workflows 01 (ingest) and 02 (router) are the backbone of that.

1. Database: stripe_events – Final, Correct Structure
In Neon, this is what we want (you already have most of it):

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events (
  id          TEXT PRIMARY KEY,          -- Stripe event id (evt_xxx)
  event_type  TEXT NOT NULL,             -- "payment_intent.succeeded", etc.
  payload     JSONB NOT NULL,            -- full Stripe event JSON
  handled     BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT FALSE,
  handled_at  TIMESTAMP NULL,
  created_at  TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
If you need to patch an existing table, this is safe to run:

ALTER TABLE stripe_events
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS event_type TEXT,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS payload JSONB,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS handled BOOLEAN DEFAULT FALSE,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS handled_at TIMESTAMP NULL,
    ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS created_at TIMESTAMP NOT NULL DEFAULT now();
✅ This matches what Workflow 01 is supposed to read/write.

2. Workflow 01 – Stripe Webhook Ingest (Final Spec)
From your screenshot, your layout is:

Webhook → Extract Event Data → Insert stripe_events → Check if Already Handled → Was Already Handled? (IF) → [false] Call '02 – Stripe Event Router' → Mark Event Handled → Respond OK

Let’s lock each node.

01-A. Webhook node
HTTP Method: POST

Path: stripe/webhook

Respond: Using ‘Respond to Webhook’ node

Production URL: the one you put in Stripe:
https://puretask.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/stripe/webhook

Stripe destination in sandbox should point to that URL (you already have this).

01-B. Extract Event Data (Code)
Mode: Run Once for All Items
Language: JavaScript

Code:

// Stripe sends the full event as the incoming JSON.
const evt = $json;

return {
  stripe_event_id: evt.id,      // "evt_..."
  event_type: evt.type,         // "payment_intent.succeeded", etc.
  payload: evt                  // full event JSON
};
After this node, each item looks like:

{
  "stripe_event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full stripe event... }
}
This is the canonical shape we’ll use everywhere.

01-C. Insert stripe_events (Postgres – executeQuery)
Query:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, event_type, payload, handled, handled_at)
VALUES ($1, $2, $3, FALSE, NULL)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;
Query Parameters (in Options → Query Parameters → Expression):

[
  $json.stripe_event_id,
  $json.event_type,
  $json.payload
]
✅ This logs every event once (idempotent by event id).
Even if Stripe retries, it won’t create a second row.

01-D. Check if Already Handled (Postgres – executeQuery)
Query:

SELECT id,
       event_type,
       payload,
       handled,
       handled_at
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Query Parameter:

[ $json.stripe_event_id ]
Important: The output of this node is an array of rows.

For a brand-new event:
[{ id, event_type, payload, handled: false, handled_at: null }]

For a replayed event:
same, but handled: true.

01-E. Was Already Handled? (IF node)
We want:

true branch → already handled → skip routing.

false branch → new event → call Workflow 02 then mark handled.

Configure the IF like this:

Value 1 (left): Expression

{{ $items("Check if Already Handled")[0].json.handled === true }}
Operation: is equal to

Value 2 (right): true

So:

If handled === true → IF condition is true → goes to true branch (direct to Respond OK).

If handled === false → IF is false → goes to false branch (Call 02 → Mark Event Handled).

If you’d rather base it on row presence:

{{ $items("Check if Already Handled").length > 0 && $items("Check if Already Handled")[0].json.handled === true }}
But from that “What’s changed” text, n8n AI already moved you to the simple handled boolean, which is what we want.

01-F. Call '02 – Stripe Event Router' (Execute Workflow)
This is where 02 was getting messed up before.
The reason your 02 input was {} is almost certainly because this node wasn’t passing through the fields correctly.

Source: Database
Workflow: 02 – Stripe Event Router
Mode: Run once with all items

Most important part – Options → Input / Data:

We want to pass the row we selected from the DB, not an empty object.

In this IF layout, the Call node is connected from Was Already Handled? (false branch), whose input is the row from Check if Already Handled.

So in Execute Workflow → Options → Input:

Leave it as default: “Use data from previous node”
(don’t override with Define Below / Manual).

To make the shape 100% correct for 02, add a small code node before Call 02, or adjust Check’s SELECT.

Cleanest option: Adjust Check query to alias columns:

SELECT id          AS event_id,
       event_type,
       payload
FROM stripe_events
WHERE id = $1;
Then 02 receives:

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full stripe event... }
}
If you do that, 02’s Normalize node can be super simple (I’ll show in the next section).

01-G. Mark Event Handled (Postgres – executeQuery)
Connected after Call 02 (success path).

Query:

UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = TRUE,
    handled_at = now()
WHERE id = $1;
Query Parameters:

[ $json.event_id || $json.stripe_event_id ]
Pick one consistent field:

If you aliased to event_id in the Check query, then:

[ $json.event_id ]
If you left it as id and didn’t alias, you’d do:

[ $json.id ]
I strongly recommend the event_id alias.

01-H. Respond OK (Respond to Webhook)
Status Code: 200

Response Body (Expression):

{{ { received: true } }}
Respond to: Webhook node.

This ensures Stripe always gets a 200 after you either process or skip (idempotent safe).

3. Workflow 02 – Stripe Event Router (Re-Audited Spec)
Goal: Take a normalized event from 01 and dispatch it to the correct processor once.

Trigger: When executed by another workflow (no webhook here).

We’ll assume 01 passes items shaped like:

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": { ...full stripe event... }
}
If your Check query doesn’t alias to event_id, you’ll tweak names below, but I’ll use this clean shape.

02-A. Incoming Event (When executed by another workflow)
Nothing fancy here; it just receives the item from 01.

02-B. Normalize Event (Code node)
Goal: produce a consistent internal shape that all processors can rely on.

Code:

const evtRow = $json;            // { event_id, event_type, payload }

const stripeEvent = evtRow.payload || evtRow;   // safety

return {
  event_id: evtRow.event_id || stripeEvent.id,
  event_type: evtRow.event_type || stripeEvent.type,
  data: stripeEvent.data || null,
  object: stripeEvent.data?.object || null,
  raw: stripeEvent
};
After this node, each item looks like:

{
  "event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "data": {
    "object": { ...payment_intent... }
    // plus other stripe data
  },
  "object": { ...payment_intent object... },
  "raw": { ...full event... }
}
This is exactly the structure processors 03–08 should expect.

02-C. Route by Event Type (Switch / IF / “Route by rules” node)
Use your existing “Route by Event Type” node, but make sure it looks at the normalized event_type:

Mode: Rules
For each rule:

payment_intent.succeeded

Condition:

Left: Expression → {{ $json.event_type }}

Operation: is equal to

Right: payment_intent.succeeded

Rename Output: ON

Output Name: payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

Same, output name: payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.created

charge.dispute.closed

payout.paid

payout.failed

Make sure the expression is exactly $json.event_type, not $json.type or anything else.

02-D. Call Processor Workflows
For each output in Route node, connect to an Execute Workflow node:

Output Name	Execute Workflow → Workflow
payment_intent.succeeded	03 – Payment Intent Succeeded Processor
payment_intent.payment_failed	04 – Payment Intent Failed Processor
charge.refunded	05 – Stripe Refund Credit Transaction Processor
charge.dispute.created	06 – Stripe Dispute Opened Event Processor
charge.dispute.closed	07 – Stripe Dispute Closed Event Processor
payout.paid	08 – Stripe Payout Paid Event Processor
payout.failed	(future) 09 – Stripe Payout Failed Processor
Each Execute Workflow node:

Source: Database

Workflow: corresponding processor

Mode: Run once with all items

Input: keep default “use data from previous node”, so the processors receive:

{
  "event_id": "...",
  "event_type": "...",
  "data": { ... },
  "object": { ... },
  "raw": { ... }
}
This gives processors everything they need to read payment intents, charges, disputes, payouts, etc., and to interact with your own tables (payment_intents, credit_transactions, clients) in a deterministic way.

4. Are We 100% Correct for PureTask (Not Just Tests)?
Let’s check against requirements:

Idempotent logging per Stripe event id

✅ stripe_events primary key on id plus ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING.

Never process the same event twice

✅ handled + handled_at updated after successful processor run in Workflow 01.

✅ Was Already Handled? reads handled and stops if true.

Router only runs on new events

✅ Only the false branch of Was Already Handled? calls Workflow 02.

Processor workflows get the right event data shape

✅ 02 Normalize node standardizes shape with event_id, event_type, data, object, raw.

Stripe gets a 200 on success + retries are safe

✅ Respond OK always sends { received: true } after logging & handling.

Works with your Stripe destination config (screen you showed)

✅ Destination points to /webhook/stripe/webhook in 01, and 01 is Active.

✅ 02 and 03+ remain Inactive at the top level (no own triggers), but they’re callable as sub-workflows — this matches the “Workflow could not be activated: has no node to start” message you saw, which is fine.

So architecturally, this is production-ready, not just “for tests”.

✔️ I see the problem clearly now — and yes, Workflow 01 is not receiving the data in the correct shape.
The error tells us exactly what’s wrong:

“null value in column ‘id’ … violating not-null constraint”

This means:

👉 Your Extract Event Data node is NOT pulling the Stripe event correctly
Instead of producing:

{
  "stripe_event_id": "evt_123",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": {...}
}
…it’s producing:

{
  "payload": {
     "body": { "id": "evt_..." }
  }
}
The stripe_event_id and event_type keys are missing, and the INSERT node receives null for id.

This is why INSERT fails.

✅ FIX THIS FIRST: Correct Extract Event Data Node
You need your Extract Event Data (Code) node to handle the exact structure Stripe sends to n8n.

Stripe ALWAYS sends webhooks as:
{
  "body": {
    "id": "evt_XXXX",
    "type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
    "data": { ... }
  }
}
So your code must correctly extract those fields.

✅ Copy/Paste This EXACT Code Into Extract Event Data
Extract Event Data – Code Node
// Stripe sends the event inside `items[0].json.body`
const event = $json.body;

return {
  stripe_event_id: event.id,
  event_type: event.type,
  payload: event        // store full stripe event object
};
Your Extract Event Data output should look like:
{
  "stripe_event_id": "evt_3SWU2BA...",
  "event_type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
  "payload": {
    "id": "evt_3SWU2BA...",
    "type": "payment_intent.succeeded",
    "data": { ... }
  }
}
If you do NOT see these keys, nothing else will work.

is it failing becuase it a test of payment_intent.succeeded, and we keep running it over and over again , would it be different if it was a real 

Short answer: no, this error is not because it’s a test payment or because you’ve run it a bunch of times. A real payment would fail in exactly the same way right now.

The problem is 100% in the Insert stripe_events node config.

What the error actually means
null value in column "type" of relation "stripe_events" violates not-null constraint

That means:

Your table stripe_events.type is NOT NULL

The row being inserted has NULL for that column

So Postgres throws this error and rejects the row

From your screenshot I can see:

Insert node INPUT (left side)
stripe_event_id  evt_3SWU2BA...
event_type       payment_intent.succeeded
payload          { ... full event ... }
So the data exists in n8n.

But the failing row (right side) looks like:
(evt_3SWU2BA..., NULL, NULL, NULL, NULL, 'payment_intent.succeeded', 2025-...)
Notice:

Column 1 (id) = correct value

Column 2 (type) = NULL ❌

Later column gets 'payment_intent.succeeded' where probably handled or handled_at should be

So your SQL parameter order doesn’t match your query. event_type isn’t being used for $2.

Fix the Insert stripe_events node
Open Insert stripe_events and set it exactly like this.

1️⃣ SQL query
INSERT INTO stripe_events (
  id,
  type,
  payload,
  job_id,
  cleaner_id,
  handled,
  handled_at
)
VALUES (
  $1,
  $2,
  $3::jsonb,
  NULL,
  NULL,
  FALSE,
  NULL
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;
If your table has fewer columns, just keep id, type, and payload for now and drop the others:

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload)
VALUES ($1, $2, $3::jsonb)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;
2️⃣ Query Parameters (this is the important bit)
In the Query Parameters section, set the expression to this exact array:

[
  {{$json.stripe_event_id}},
  {{$json.event_type}},
  {{$json.payload}}
]
$1 → stripe_event_id

$2 → event_type

$3 → payload

Right now you almost certainly have them in the wrong order (e.g. [event_id, payload, event_type]), which is why type is coming through as null.

About “running the same test payment over and over”
With the correct SQL and ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING:

The first time Stripe sends evt_3SW... → it will insert the row

Any retries / repeats of the same event id → Postgres will just skip (DO NOTHING)

No error, no duplicate rows

So reusing the same test event is fine and is exactly how Stripe recommends testing webhooks.

Right now you’re not even getting that far — the insert fails before the conflict rule matters, because type is null.

What to do next
Fix Insert stripe_events SQL + Query Parameters as above

Resend a payment_intent.succeeded event from Stripe

Check:

Insert stripe_events node → should be green

Neon console → SELECT * FROM stripe_events ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC LIMIT 5;
You should see your event with both id and type populated.

Once that’s working, Workflow 01 is in good shape and we can finish tightening up Workflow 02 so PureTask is ready for real traffic.

FROM stripe_events

❗ WAIT — Important check
Your stripe_events table might not have created_at_utc (depending on how it was originally created).

If you're not sure, run this instead:

FROM stripe_events
ORDER BY created_at DESC NULLS LAST
LIMIT 5;
or this safe universal version:

SELECT *
FROM stripe_events
ORDER BY 1 DESC
LIMIT 5;
But ideally, your table should have these columns:

column	type	required
id	text	YES (PK)
type	text	YES
payload	jsonb	YES
handled	boolean	defaults to false
handled_at	timestamp	null
created_at_utc	timestamp	default now()
If you want your table to ALWAYS store an auto timestamp, run this:

ALTER TABLE stripe_events
ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS created_at_utc TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW();

This is NOT an error

do we have any of the following complete or wired or in our database at all? - SECTION 10 — VALIDATION RULES (PER EVENT, BACKEND + N8N)

This is the rulebook that keeps your job lifecycle correct and your data clean.

🎯 Section 10 – Goals

By the end of this section, a freelancer should:

Know exactly what must be validated in the backend before emitting an event.

Know what n8n should validate again (belt + suspenders).

Understand per-event rules (who can do what, when).

Understand the job status state machine (what transitions are allowed).

Have patterns for implementing these checks in TypeScript and n8n Function nodes.

This prevents:

illegal status jumps (requested → completed directly)

cleaners checking in on jobs they don’t own

clients approving jobs that aren’t ready

random/typo event_names from entering the pipeline

10.1 Two-Layer Validation Philosophy

We use two layers:

Backend validation (authoritative, strict)

Enforces business logic and permissions.

Checks job state, ownership, payload completeness.

Decides if the action is allowed at all.

n8n validation (defensive, schema-focused)

Ensures the incoming event JSON is structurally valid.

Protects the event log (job_events) from bad data.

Keeps automations safe from malformed events.

Think of it like:

Backend = “Am I allowed to do this?”
n8n = “Is this event envelope well-formed & allowed?”

10.2 Global Backend Validation Rules

These apply to every job-related action in the backend:

Auth required.
Every request must be made by an authenticated user.

Ownership / permission check.

For cleaner actions: user must map to the relevant cleaners row, and job.cleaner_id must match or be assignable.

For client actions: user must map to the relevant customers row, and job.client_id must match.

Job existence.
job_id must exist in jobs.

Job not soft-deleted / archived.
Jobs marked as deleted/archived should not accept lifecycle events.

Status precondition.
The job must be in a status where this action is valid (state machine).

Payload fields.
Any required payload fields must be present (GPS, notes, rating, etc., per event).

Only after this passes do we:

Update DB state

Emit the event via publishEvent()

10.3 Global n8n Validation Rules

In your Validate Event Envelope Function node (Section 8), n8n should:

Ensure required top-level fields exist:

event_name

job_id

payload (object)

Ensure event_name is in the allowed list.

Ensure cleaner_id / client_id are present when required.

Optionally: ensure payload conforms to some basic expectations (types, minimal fields).

Normalize:

source (default backend)

occurred_at (default now)

n8n does not verify job state or ownership; that’s backend’s job.

10.4 State Machine – Allowed Job Status Transitions

Let’s define a simple v1 state machine. Backends must enforce this.

From Status	Event Name	To Status
(none/new row)	job.created	requested
requested	job.cleaner_accepted	accepted
accepted	job.cleaner_on_my_way (optional)	on_my_way
accepted/on_my_way	job.cleaner_checked_in	in_progress
in_progress	job.cleaner_checked_out	in_progress
in_progress	job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval	awaiting_approval
awaiting_approval	job.client_approved	completed
awaiting_approval	job.client_disputed	disputed
many states	job.cancelled	cancelled / no_show

Backend rule:

Reject any request that would cause an illegal transition.

Example:

You cannot approve a job (job.client_approved) if status is still requested.

10.5 Per-Event Validation Rules (Backend)

We’ll go event by event.

1) job.created

Triggered by: client
Route: POST /jobs

Backend must validate:

User is authenticated.

User is allowed to be a client.

Client exists (customers row).

Required body fields present:

scheduled_start

estimated_hours

base price inputs (if needed for total_credits)

Client has enough credits (later, when credit system in place).

No conflicting job scheduled for the same slot (optional rule).

If valid:

Insert jobs row with:

status = 'requested'

total_credits

Emit job.created event.

2) job.cleaner_accepted

Triggered by: cleaner
Route: POST /jobs/:id/accept

Backend must validate:

User is authenticated.

User maps to cleaner_id.

Job exists.

Job is in requested status.

Job not already assigned to another cleaner (unless multi-accept, but we assume not for v1).

Cleaner meets any tier requirements (optional future rule).

If valid:

Set jobs.cleaner_id = cleaner.id

Set jobs.status = 'accepted'

Emit job.cleaner_accepted.

3) job.cleaner_on_my_way

Triggered by: cleaner
Route: POST /jobs/:id/on-my-way

Backend must validate:

User is authenticated, is that job’s cleaner.

Job is in accepted status (not yet in progress).

Provided gps_lat / gps_lng are numbers.

Optional:

Prevent spamming “on my way” multiple times (or allow but only the first matters).

If valid:

Optional: jobs.status = 'on_my_way'

Emit job.cleaner_on_my_way.

4) job.cleaner_checked_in

Triggered by: cleaner
Route: POST /jobs/:id/check-in

Backend must validate:

Auth user = job.cleaner.

Job exists.

Job is in accepted or on_my_way status.

Time window:

Not too early (e.g., not >X minutes before scheduled_start).

Not too late (for reliability scoring).

Payload:

gps_lat / gps_lng present and valid.

If valid:

jobs.status = 'in_progress'

Optional: store check_in_time.

Emit job.cleaner_checked_in.

5) job.cleaner_checked_out

Triggered by: cleaner
Route: POST /jobs/:id/check-out

Backend must validate:

Auth user = job.cleaner.

Job exists.

Job is in in_progress status.

Optional: ensure check-in happened first.

Payload:

gps_lat / gps_lng valid.

Optional actual_hours consistent with time between check-in & check-out.

If valid:

Keep jobs.status = 'in_progress' (job isn’t complete yet).

Optional: store check_out_time.

Emit job.cleaner_checked_out.

6) job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval

Triggered by: cleaner
Route: POST /jobs/:id/submit-for-approval

Backend must validate:

Auth user = job.cleaner.

Job exists.

Job is in in_progress status.

Optional: ensure check-out happened.

Payload:

photos exist (array, can be empty but usually should have at least 1).

notes exists (string, possibly empty).

If valid:

jobs.status = 'awaiting_approval'

Emit job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval.

7) job.client_approved

Triggered by: client
Route: POST /jobs/:id/approve

Backend must validate:

Auth user = job.client.

Job exists.

Job is in awaiting_approval status.

Ensure job has proper check-in/out & submission events (optional enforcement).

Payload:

rating (optional but validated if present)

feedback (optional)

If valid:

jobs.status = 'completed'

Later: move escrow → cleaner earnings.

Emit job.client_approved.

8) job.client_disputed

Triggered by: client
Route: POST /jobs/:id/dispute

Backend must validate:

Auth user = job.client.

Job exists.

Job is in awaiting_approval status.

Payload:

reason required.

photos optional.

requested_resolution optional.

If valid:

jobs.status = 'disputed'

Emit job.client_disputed.

9) job.cancelled

Triggered by: client / cleaner / system
Route examples:

POST /jobs/:id/cancel (client or cleaner)

System may call an internal method (no HTTP route) if auto-cancel.

Backend must validate:

Job exists.

Job status is one of: requested, accepted, on_my_way, maybe in_progress (policy choice).

Identify cancelled_by:

If client:

Auth user = client

cancelled_by = "client"

If cleaner:

Auth user = cleaner

cancelled_by = "cleaner"

If system:

internal call, cancelled_by = "system"

Determine policy/penalty based on:

When the cancellation happened.

Who canceled.

Job tier, etc. (later sections).

If valid:

jobs.status = 'cancelled' or no_show.

Emit job.cancelled event with:

payload.cancelled_by

payload.policy_tier

payload.reason (optional)

10.6 n8n-Side Per-Event Validation (Light Version)

You don’t want to reimplement full business logic in n8n, but you can enforce minimal conditions per event_name in the Validate Event Envelope Function node:

Example snippet:

switch (body.event_name) {
  case "job.cleaner_accepted":
  case "job.cleaner_on_my_way":
  case "job.cleaner_checked_in":
  case "job.cleaner_checked_out":
  case "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval":
    if (!body.cleaner_id) {
      throw new Error(${body.event_name}: cleaner_id is required);
    }
    break;

  case "job.client_approved":
  case "job.client_disputed":
    if (!body.client_id) {
      throw new Error(${body.event_name}: client_id is required);
    }
    break;

  case "job.cancelled":
    if (!body.payload.cancelled_by) {
      throw new Error("job.cancelled: payload.cancelled_by is required");
    }
    break;
}


Backend already enforces this, but n8n double-checks to keep job_events clean.

10.7 Error Responses (Backend)

You want clear, consistent errors for bad actions.

Example structure:

{
  "error": {
    "code": "INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION",
    "message": "Cannot check in a job that is not accepted or on_my_way.",
    "details": {
      "job_id": "0000...",
      "current_status": "requested",
      "required_statuses": ["accepted", "on_my_way"]
    }
  }
}


Common error codes:

JOB_NOT_FOUND

FORBIDDEN_JOB_ACCESS

INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION

MISSING_REQUIRED_FIELD

INSUFFICIENT_CREDITS (later)

ALREADY_COMPLETED

These make debugging so much easier.

10.8 Validation Summary Matrix

Here’s a compact view for devs:

Event Name	Who	From Status → To	Required IDs	Key Payload Requirements
job.created	C	(none) → requested	client_id	scheduled_start, estimated_hours, total_credits
job.cleaner_accepted	Cln	requested → accepted	cleaner_id	–
job.cleaner_on_my_way	Cln	accepted → on_my_way	cleaner_id	gps_lat, gps_lng (if used)
job.cleaner_checked_in	Cln	accepted/on_my_way → in_progress	cleaner_id	gps_lat, gps_lng
job.cleaner_checked_out	Cln	in_progress → in_progress	cleaner_id	gps_lat, gps_lng, actual_hours?
job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval	Cln	in_progress → awaiting_approval	cleaner_id	photos?, notes
job.client_approved	C	awaiting_approval → completed	client_id	final_credits_charged
job.client_disputed	C	awaiting_approval → disputed	client_id	reason
job.cancelled	C/Cln/System	many → cancelled	client_id/cleaner_id (depending)	cancelled_by, reason?, policy_tier?

(C = client, Cln = cleaner)

3. Step-by-step: how to build what’s missing
I’ll give you an opinionated blueprint you can literally follow.

PHASE A – Create the job lifecycle tables in Neon
A1. Create a status enum
In Neon’s SQL Editor:

-- 1) Job status enum
CREATE TYPE job_status AS ENUM (
  'requested',
  'accepted',
  'on_my_way',
  'in_progress',
  'awaiting_approval',
  'completed',
  'disputed',
  'cancelled',
  'no_show'
);
Run that once. If you re-run and it says “already exists”, that’s fine.

A2. Create jobs table
Still in Neon SQL Editor:

CREATE TABLE jobs (
  id               UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  client_id        UUID NOT NULL,
  cleaner_id       UUID, -- can be null until someone accepts
  status           job_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'requested',

  scheduled_start  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  estimated_hours  NUMERIC(5,2),

  total_credits    INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

  created_at       TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at       TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),

  -- soft delete flags if you want later
  deleted_at       TIMESTAMPTZ
);
You can extend later (address, notes, etc.), but this is enough to support the state machine.

A3. Create job_events table
CREATE TABLE job_events (
  id           UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
  job_id       UUID NOT NULL REFERENCES jobs(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,

  event_name   TEXT NOT NULL,     -- e.g. 'job.cleaner_accepted'
  actor_type   TEXT NOT NULL,     -- 'client' | 'cleaner' | 'system'
  actor_id     UUID,              -- who did it (nullable for system)

  payload      JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,

  occurred_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  created_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

-- Helpful indexes
CREATE INDEX idx_job_events_job_id_created_at
  ON job_events(job_id, created_at);

CREATE INDEX idx_job_events_event_name
  ON job_events(event_name);
Now you have the storage for:

current job state (jobs.status)

full event history (job_events)

PHASE B – Decide & access your backend
I’ll assume base44 is a Next.js + TypeScript project (common pattern). If it’s something else, the logic is the same, only routing differs.

B1. Open the backend project
Unzip base44.

Open it in VS Code.

In a terminal in that folder:

npm install
npm run dev
Visit http://localhost:3000 – if you see a site, this is the frontend + backend (Next.js).

B2. Configure DB connection
You need your Neon connection string (already used by n8n). Put it in an env var, e.g.:

.env.local:

DATABASE_URL=postgresql://user:password@host:port/dbname
Then:

Either use an ORM (Prisma, Drizzle) or

Use pg (node-postgres) directly.

Example with pg:

// lib/db.ts
import { Pool } from "pg";

export const pool = new Pool({
  connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL,
});
Now any API route can do const client = await pool.connect() and query Neon.

PHASE C – Implement the job state machine in the backend
We’ll do minimal endpoints for v1.

C1. Define allowed transitions in one place
Create lib/jobStateMachine.ts:

export type JobStatus =
  | "requested"
  | "accepted"
  | "on_my_way"
  | "in_progress"
  | "awaiting_approval"
  | "completed"
  | "disputed"
  | "cancelled"
  | "no_show";

type Transition = {
  from: JobStatus[];
  to: JobStatus;
  event: string;
};

export const transitions: Transition[] = [
  { from: ["requested"], to: "accepted", event: "job.cleaner_accepted" },
  { from: ["accepted"], to: "on_my_way", event: "job.cleaner_on_my_way" },
  { from: ["accepted", "on_my_way"], to: "in_progress", event: "job.cleaner_checked_in" },
  { from: ["in_progress"], to: "in_progress", event: "job.cleaner_checked_out" },
  { from: ["in_progress"], to: "awaiting_approval", event: "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval" },
  { from: ["awaiting_approval"], to: "completed", event: "job.client_approved" },
  { from: ["awaiting_approval"], to: "disputed", event: "job.client_disputed" },
  { from: ["requested","accepted","on_my_way","in_progress"], to: "cancelled", event: "job.cancelled" },
];

export function getAllowedTransition(
  currentStatus: JobStatus,
  eventName: string
): Transition | null {
  return (
    transitions.find(
      (t) => t.event === eventName && t.from.includes(currentStatus)
    ) || null
  );
}
This is your truth for allowed jumps.

C2. Implement publishJobEvent helper
lib/publishJobEvent.ts:

import { pool } from "./db";
import type { JobStatus } from "./jobStateMachine";
import { getAllowedTransition } from "./jobStateMachine";

type ActorType = "client" | "cleaner" | "system";

export async function publishJobEvent(params: {
  jobId: string;
  eventName: string;
  actorType: ActorType;
  actorId?: string;
  payload?: any;
}) {
  const { jobId, eventName, actorType, actorId, payload = {} } = params;
  const client = await pool.connect();

  try {
    await client.query("BEGIN");

    // 1) Load current job to know its status
    const jobRes = await client.query(
      `SELECT status FROM jobs WHERE id = $1 FOR UPDATE`,
      [jobId]
    );
    if (jobRes.rowCount === 0) {
      throw {
        code: "JOB_NOT_FOUND",
        message: "Job not found",
      };
    }

    const currentStatus = jobRes.rows[0].status as JobStatus;

    // 2) Check allowed transition
    const transition = getAllowedTransition(currentStatus, eventName);
    if (!transition) {
      throw {
        code: "INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION",
        message: `Cannot apply ${eventName} from status ${currentStatus}`,
        details: { jobId, currentStatus },
      };
    }

    // 3) Update job status if it changes
    if (transition.to !== currentStatus) {
      await client.query(
        `UPDATE jobs
         SET status = $1,
             updated_at = now()
         WHERE id = $2`,
        [transition.to, jobId]
      );
    }

    // 4) Insert job_events record
    await client.query(
      `INSERT INTO job_events (
        job_id, event_name, actor_type, actor_id, payload
      )
       VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, $5::jsonb)`,
      [jobId, eventName, actorType, actorId ?? null, JSON.stringify(payload)]
    );

    await client.query("COMMIT");
  } catch (err) {
    await client.query("ROLLBACK");
    throw err;
  } finally {
    client.release();
  }
}
Now every endpoint can:

Do auth + ownership checks

Call publishJobEvent({ ... })

That function enforces the state machine and records the event.

C3. Example endpoint: job.cleaner_accepted
In Next.js App Router, for example: app/api/jobs/[id]/accept/route.ts:

import { NextRequest, NextResponse } from "next/server";
import { pool } from "@/lib/db";
import { publishJobEvent } from "@/lib/publishJobEvent";

export async function POST(
  req: NextRequest,
  { params }: { params: { id: string } }
) {
  const jobId = params.id;
  const userId = "TODO-get-from-auth"; // from your auth system
  const cleanerId = userId;            // assuming 1:1 mapping for now

  const client = await pool.connect();

  try {
    // 1) Ensure job exists and is not deleted
    const jobRes = await client.query(
      `SELECT id, status, cleaner_id FROM jobs WHERE id = $1`,
      [jobId]
    );
    if (jobRes.rowCount === 0) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: { code: "JOB_NOT_FOUND" } },
        { status: 404 }
      );
    }

    const job = jobRes.rows[0];

    // 2) Ensure not already assigned to another cleaner
    if (job.cleaner_id && job.cleaner_id !== cleanerId) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: { code: "FORBIDDEN_JOB_ACCESS", message: "Job already assigned" } },
        { status: 403 }
      );
    }

    // 3) Assign cleaner
    await client.query(
      `UPDATE jobs
       SET cleaner_id = $1, updated_at = now()
       WHERE id = $2`,
      [cleanerId, jobId]
    );

    // 4) Publish event (this enforces status transition)
    await publishJobEvent({
      jobId,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_accepted",
      actorType: "cleaner",
      actorId: cleanerId,
      payload: {},
    });

    return NextResponse.json({ ok: true });
  } catch (err: any) {
    console.error(err);
    const code = err.code ?? "UNKNOWN_ERROR";
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: { code, message: err.message ?? "Something went wrong" } },
      { status: 400 }
    );
  } finally {
    client.release();
  }
}
You’d repeat this pattern for:

/api/jobs (job.created)

/api/jobs/[id]/on-my-way

/api/jobs/[id]/check-in

/api/jobs/[id]/check-out

/api/jobs/[id]/submit-for-approval

/api/jobs/[id]/approve

/api/jobs/[id]/dispute

/api/jobs/[id]/cancel

Each one:

Auth check (client vs cleaner).

Ownership check (job.client_id / job.cleaner_id).

Any required payload fields.

Call publishJobEvent with the correct eventName & payload.

PHASE D – n8n ingestion of job events (Section 10 style)
Right now n8n ingests Stripe events. We eventually want n8n to also ingest job. events* from your backend.

D1. Create a new workflow in n8n: “03 – Job Event Ingest”
Add a Webhook node

Method: POST

Path: /webhook/job-events (example)

Add a Function node “Validate Job Event Envelope”:

Code example:

const body = $json;

const allowedEvents = [
  "job.created",
  "job.cleaner_accepted",
  "job.cleaner_on_my_way",
  "job.cleaner_checked_in",
  "job.cleaner_checked_out",
  "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval",
  "job.client_approved",
  "job.client_disputed",
  "job.cancelled",
];

if (!body.event_name || !allowedEvents.includes(body.event_name)) {
  throw new Error(`Invalid event_name: ${body.event_name}`);
}

if (!body.job_id) {
  throw new Error("job_id is required");
}

if ([
  "job.cleaner_accepted",
  "job.cleaner_on_my_way",
  "job.cleaner_checked_in",
  "job.cleaner_checked_out",
  "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval",
].includes(body.event_name)) {
  if (!body.cleaner_id) {
    throw new Error(`${body.event_name}: cleaner_id is required`);
  }
}

if ([
  "job.client_approved",
  "job.client_disputed",
].includes(body.event_name)) {
  if (!body.client_id) {
    throw new Error(`${body.event_name}: client_id is required`);
  }
}

if (body.event_name === "job.cancelled") {
  if (!body.payload || !body.payload.cancelled_by) {
    throw new Error("job.cancelled: payload.cancelled_by is required");
  }
}

// Normalize
return [
  {
    json: {
      event_name: body.event_name,
      job_id: body.job_id,
      cleaner_id: body.cleaner_id ?? null,
      client_id: body.client_id ?? null,
      payload: body.payload ?? {},
      source: body.source ?? "backend",
      occurred_at: body.occurred_at ?? new Date().toISOString(),
    },
  },
];
Add a Postgres node to insert into job_events if you want n8n to also log events (optional, since backend already does).

Or you can just let n8n react to events (send notifications, etc.) using a Router node based on event_name.

D2. Backend → n8n call
In publishJobEvent, after inserting into DB, you can fetch the n8n webhook URL (/webhook/job-events) with the same JSON.

Later we can wire that in more detail.

FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_name = 'jobs'
ORDER BY ordinal_position;
Replace 'jobs' with 'job_events', 'stripe_events', etc.

If this returns rows → the table exists and you see columns.

If you get relation "jobs" does not exist → the table is missing.

SELECT *
FROM jobs
ORDER BY created_at DESC
LIMIT 5;
Same thing for job_events, stripe_events, etc.

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS jobs (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),

    client_id TEXT NOT NULL,
    cleaner_id TEXT,

    status TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'requested',

    scheduled_start TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
    estimated_hours INTEGER NOT NULL,

    total_credits INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,

    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);
4️⃣ Create job_events
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_events (
    id UUID PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid(),
    job_id UUID NOT NULL,
    event_name TEXT NOT NULL,
    payload JSONB NOT NULL,
    cleaner_id TEXT,
    client_id TEXT,
    source TEXT DEFAULT 'backend',
    occurred_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW(),
    created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NOW()
);

✅ job_events schema check
From your screenshot, job_events is:

Table "public.job_events"
  Column      | Type                       | Nullable | Default
--------------+----------------------------+----------+-------------------
  id          | uuid                       | not null | gen_random_uuid()
  job_id      | uuid                       | not null | 
  event_name  | text                       | not null | 
  payload     | jsonb                      | not null | 
  cleaner_id  | text                       |          | 
  client_id   | text                       |          | 
  source      | text                       |          | 'backend'::text
  occurred_at | timestamp with time zone   |          | now()
  created_at  | timestamp with time zone   |          | now()
Indexes:
  "job_events_pkey" PRIMARY KEY, btree (id)
That is spot-on for what we designed:

id – unique event id (auto-generated)

job_id – which job this event belongs to

event_name – e.g. job.created, job.cleaner_accepted

payload – extra details (GPS, notes, etc.) as JSON

cleaner_id / client_id – who did it (optional per event)

source – usually 'backend' (later we could have n8n, script, etc.)

occurred_at – when it happened (business time)

created_at – when we stored it in the DB

If the other 3 tables look similar (proper columns, defaults, etc.), then your core event schema is ready to use.

Quick sanity test for each table (optional but good)

1. Pick the stack (I’ll assume Node + Express)

Node.js

dotenv (for secrets/env vars)

You don’t need TypeScript yet – we can always add it later.

2. Create the project
In a new folder (e.g. puretask-backend):

mkdir puretask-backend
cd puretask-backend
npm init -y

npm install express pg cors dotenv
This gives you a basic Node project.

3. Add .env with your Neon connection
In the root of puretask-backend, create .env:

PORT=4000

DATABASE_URL=postgresql://USER:PASSWORD@HOST:PORT/DATABASE
You can grab this full connection string from your Neon console (“Connect” → “Connection string”).
Make sure it points to the same branch (development) and same DB where you saw:

stripe_events

payment_intents

jobs

job_events

4. Create db.js (database helper)
Create db.js:

// db.js
require('dotenv').config();
const { Pool } = require('pg');

if (!process.env.DATABASE_URL) {
  throw new Error('DATABASE_URL is not set in .env');
}

const pool = new Pool({
  connectionString: process.env.DATABASE_URL,
});

module.exports = {
  query: (text, params) => pool.query(text, params),
  getClient: () => pool.connect(),
};
This lets us run queries easily and open transactions.

5. Create server.js with first endpoint
Create server.js:

// server.js
require('dotenv').config();
const express = require('express');
const cors = require('cors');
const db = require('./db');

const app = express();
const PORT = process.env.PORT || 4000;

app.use(cors());
app.use(express.json());

// Health check
app.get('/health', (req, res) => {
  res.json({ ok: true, service: 'puretask-backend' });
});

/**
 * POST /jobs
 * Body: {
 *   client_id: string,
 *   scheduled_start: string (ISO datetime),
 *   estimated_hours: number,
 *   total_credits: number
 * }
 *
 * Behavior:
 *   1) Insert row into jobs with status='requested'
 *   2) Insert job.created event into job_events
 */
app.post('/jobs', async (req, res) => {
  const { client_id, scheduled_start, estimated_hours, total_credits } = req.body;

  // Basic validation (backend-level, we’ll expand this later)
  if (!client_id || !scheduled_start || !estimated_hours || !total_credits) {
    return res.status(400).json({
      error: {
        code: 'MISSING_REQUIRED_FIELD',
        message: 'client_id, scheduled_start, estimated_hours, and total_credits are required.',
      },
    });
  }

  const client = await db.getClient();

  try {
    await client.query('BEGIN');

    // 1) Insert job row
    const insertJobSql = `
      INSERT INTO jobs (
        client_id,
        status,
        scheduled_start,
        estimated_hours,
        total_credits
      )
      VALUES ($1, 'requested', $2, $3, $4)
      RETURNING id, status, scheduled_start, estimated_hours, total_credits, created_at;
    `;

    const jobResult = await client.query(insertJobSql, [
      client_id,
      scheduled_start,
      estimated_hours,
      total_credits,
    ]);

    const job = jobResult.rows[0];

    // 2) Insert job.created event
    const insertEventSql = `
      INSERT INTO job_events (
        job_id,
        event_name,
        payload,
        client_id,
        source,
        occurred_at
      )
      VALUES ($1, $2, $3, $4, 'backend', NOW())
      RETURNING id, job_id, event_name, occurred_at, created_at;
    `;

    const payload = {
      scheduled_start: job.scheduled_start,
      estimated_hours: job.estimated_hours,
      total_credits: job.total_credits,
      status: job.status,
    };

    const eventResult = await client.query(insertEventSql, [
      job.id,
      'job.created',
      payload,
      client_id,
    ]);

    const event = eventResult.rows[0];

    await client.query('COMMIT');

    return res.status(201).json({
      job,
      event,
    });
  } catch (err) {
    await client.query('ROLLBACK');
    console.error('Error in POST /jobs:', err);

    return res.status(500).json({
      error: {
        code: 'INTERNAL_ERROR',
        message: 'Failed to create job.',
      },
    });
  } finally {
    client.release();
  }
});

app.listen(PORT, () => {
  console.log(`PureTask backend listening on http://localhost:${PORT}`);
});
⚠️ Note:
If your jobs column names differ (client_id type, scheduled_at instead of scheduled_start, etc.), this INSERT may error. If it does, show me the error and we’ll adjust the SQL to match your exact schema.

6. Add start script and run it
In package.json, add a start script:

{
  "name": "puretask-backend",
  "version": "1.0.0",
  "main": "server.js",
  "scripts": {
    "start": "node server.js"
  },
  "dependencies": {
    "cors": "^2.8.5",
    "dotenv": "^16.0.0",
    "express": "^4.18.0",
    "pg": "^8.11.0"
  }
}
Then run:

npm start
You should see:

PureTask backend listening on http://localhost:4000
7. Test the endpoint
Use Postman, Insomnia or just curl:

curl -X POST http://localhost:4000/jobs \
  -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
  -d '{
    "client_id": "client_123",
    "scheduled_start": "2025-12-01T15:00:00Z",
    "estimated_hours": 2,
    "total_credits": 50
  }'
If everything’s hooked up, you’ll get back JSON like:

{
  "job": {
    "id": "some-uuid",
    "status": "requested",
    "scheduled_start": "2025-12-01T15:00:00.000Z",
    "estimated_hours": 2,
    "total_credits": 50,
    "created_at": "..."
  },
  "event": {
    "id": "event-uuid",
    "job_id": "some-uuid",
    "event_name": "job.created",
    "occurred_at": "...",
    "created_at": "..."
  }
}
Then in Neon, you can verify:

You should see your new job and the job.created event.

🚀 PART 6 — State Machine (critical) → src/utils/stateMachine.ts
export const allowedTransitions: any = {
  "requested": ["accepted", "cancelled"],
  "accepted": ["on_my_way", "in_progress", "cancelled"],
  "on_my_way": ["in_progress", "cancelled"],
  "in_progress": ["awaiting_approval", "cancelled"],
  "awaiting_approval": ["completed", "disputed", "cancelled"],
};

export function validateTransition(current: string, next: string) {
  const allowed = allowedTransitions[current] || [];
  if (!allowed.includes(next)) {
    throw new Error(`Invalid status transition: ${current} → ${next}`);
  }
}
🚀 PART 7 — Universal Event Emitter (backend → n8n) → src/utils/eventEmitter.ts
import axios from "axios";

export async function emitEvent(event: any) {
  try {
    await axios.post(
      "https://puretasek.app.n8n.cloud/webhook/event-ingest",
      event
    );
  } catch (err) {
    console.error("Failed to emit event:", err);
  }
}
🚀 PART 8 — VALIDATION → src/utils/validate.ts
export function requireFields(body: any, fields: string[]) {
  for (const f of fields) {
    if (body[f] === undefined || body[f] === null) {
      throw new Error(`Missing required field: ${f}`);
    }
  }
}
🚀 PART 9 — AUTH MIDDLEWARE → src/middleware/auth.ts
(Temporary easy JWT system)

import jwt from "jsonwebtoken";

export function auth(req: any, res: any, next: any) {
  const token = req.headers.authorization?.split(" ")[1];
  if (!token) return res.status(401).json({ error: "Unauthorized" });

  try {
    req.user = jwt.verify(token, process.env.JWT_SECRET!);
    next();
  } catch (e) {
    return res.status(401).json({ error: "Invalid token" });
  }
}
🚀 PART 10 — JOBS SERVICE (business logic) → src/services/jobsService.ts
This is where the magic happens.

import { db } from "../db";
import { validateTransition } from "../utils/stateMachine";
import { emitEvent } from "../utils/eventEmitter";

export async function updateJobStatus(job_id: string, nextStatus: string, payload: any, user: any) {

  const jobRes = await db.query("SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id=$1", [job_id]);
  if (jobRes.rowCount === 0) throw new Error("Job not found");

  const job = jobRes.rows[0];

  validateTransition(job.status, nextStatus);

  await db.query(
    "UPDATE jobs SET status=$1 WHERE id=$2",
    [nextStatus, job_id]
  );

  await db.query(
    `INSERT INTO job_events (job_id, event_name, payload, cleaner_id, client_id)
     VALUES ($1,$2,$3,$4,$5)`,
    [job_id, `job.${nextStatus}`, payload, user.cleaner_id, user.client_id]
  );

  await emitEvent({
    job_id,
    event_name: `job.${nextStatus}`,
    payload,
    cleaner_id: user.cleaner_id,
    client_id: user.client_id
  });

  return { success: true };
}
🚀 PART 11 — JOBS CONTROLLER → src/controllers/jobsController.ts
import { updateJobStatus } from "../services/jobsService";
import { requireFields } from "../utils/validate";

export async function cleanerAccept(req: any, res: any) {
  try {
    requireFields(req.body, ["job_id"]);

    const result = await updateJobStatus(
      req.body.job_id,
      "accepted",
      {},
      req.user
    );

    res.json(result);
  } catch (e: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: e.message });
  }
}

🚀 PART 13 — STRIPE WEBHOOK HANDLER → src/controllers/stripeController.ts
import Stripe from "stripe";
import { db } from "../db";

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY!);

export async function stripeWebhook(req: any, res: any) {
  const sig = req.headers["stripe-signature"];
  let event;

  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(
      req.rawBody,
      sig!,
      process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET!
    );
  } catch (err: any) {
    return res.status(400).send(`Webhook Error: ${err.message}`);
  }

  await db.query(
    `INSERT INTO stripe_events (stripe_event_id, type, payload)
     VALUES ($1,$2,$3)`,
    [event.id, event.type, event.data.object]
  );

  return res.json({ received: true });
}

# src/state/jobStateMachine.ts
write("src/state/jobStateMachine.ts", """
export type JobStatus =
  | "requested"
  | "accepted"
  | "on_my_way"
  | "in_progress"
  | "awaiting_approval"
  | "completed"
  | "disputed"
  | "cancelled"
  | "no_show";

export type JobEventName =
  | "job.created"
  | "job.cleaner_accepted"
  | "job.cleaner_on_my_way"
  | "job.cleaner_checked_in"
  | "job.cleaner_checked_out"
  | "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval"
  | "job.client_approved"
  | "job.client_disputed"
  | "job.cancelled";

const transitions: Record<JobStatus | "none", Partial<Record<JobEventName, JobStatus>>> = {
  none: {
    "job.created": "requested"
  },
  requested: {
    "job.cleaner_accepted": "accepted",
    "job.cancelled": "cancelled"
  },
  accepted: {
    "job.cleaner_on_my_way": "on_my_way",
    "job.cleaner_checked_in": "in_progress",
    "job.cancelled": "cancelled"
  },
  on_my_way: {
    "job.cleaner_checked_in": "in_progress",
    "job.cancelled": "cancelled"
  },
  in_progress: {
    "job.cleaner_checked_out": "in_progress",
    "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval": "awaiting_approval",
    "job.cancelled": "cancelled"
  },
  awaiting_approval: {
    "job.client_approved": "completed",
    "job.client_disputed": "disputed",
    "job.cancelled": "cancelled"
  },
  completed: {},
  disputed: {},
  cancelled: {},
  no_show: {}
};

export function getNextStatus(current: JobStatus | "none", event: JobEventName): JobStatus | null {
  return transitions[current]?.[event] ?? null;
}
""")

# src/services/eventsService.ts
write("src/services/eventsService.ts", """
import { query } from "../db/client";
import type { JobEventName } from "../state/jobStateMachine";

export interface PublishEventInput {
  jobId: string;
  eventName: JobEventName;
  payload: any;
  cleanerId?: string | null;
  clientId?: string | null;
  source?: string;
  occurredAt?: Date;
}

/**
 * Inserts a row into job_events and returns it.
 */
export async function publishEvent(input: PublishEventInput) {
  const {
    jobId,
    eventName,
    payload,
    cleanerId = null,
    clientId = null,
    source = "backend",
    occurredAt = new Date()
  } = input;

  const result = await query(
    `
    INSERT INTO job_events (job_id, event_name, payload, cleaner_id, client_id, source, occurred_at)
    VALUES ($1, $2, $3::jsonb, $4, $5, $6, $7)
    RETURNING *;
    `,
    [jobId, eventName, JSON.stringify(payload ?? {}), cleanerId, clientId, source, occurredAt]
  );

  return result.rows[0];
}
""")

# src/services/jobsService.ts
write("src/services/jobsService.ts", """
import { query } from "../db/client";
import { getNextStatus, type JobStatus, type JobEventName } from "../state/jobStateMachine";
import { publishEvent } from "./eventsService";

export interface JobRow {
  id: string;
  client_id: string;
  cleaner_id: string | null;
  status: JobStatus;
  scheduled_start: Date;
  estimated_hours: number;
  total_credits: number;
}

/**
 * Fetch a job by id.
 */
export async function getJob(jobId: string): Promise<JobRow | null> {
  const res = await query<JobRow>("SELECT * FROM jobs WHERE id = $1", [jobId]);
  return res.rows[0] ?? null;
}

/**
 * Update job status with state-machine validation and emit event.
 */
export async function applyJobEvent(options: {
  jobId: string;
  currentStatus: JobStatus | "none";
  eventName: JobEventName;
  payload: any;
  cleanerId?: string | null;
  clientId?: string | null;
}) {
  const { jobId, currentStatus, eventName, payload, cleanerId, clientId } = options;

  const nextStatus = getNextStatus(currentStatus, eventName);
  if (!nextStatus) {
    throw new Error(`INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION: cannot apply ${eventName} from status ${currentStatus}`);
  }

  // Update job
  await query(
    `
    UPDATE jobs
    SET status = $2,
        cleaner_id = COALESCE($3, cleaner_id),
        updated_at = now()
    WHERE id = $1
    `,
    [jobId, nextStatus, cleanerId ?? null]
  );

  // Emit event
  const event = await publishEvent({
    jobId,
    eventName,
    payload,
    cleanerId: cleanerId ?? undefined,
    clientId: clientId ?? undefined
  });

  return { nextStatus, event };
}
""")

# src/middleware/auth.ts (stub)
write("src/middleware/auth.ts", """
import { Request, Response, NextFunction } from "express";

/**
 * Super simple auth stub.
 *
 * In a real deployment you would:
 * - Validate a JWT / Clerk Session / Supabase auth
 * - Look up the user in your `clients` / `cleaners` tables
 * - Attach `req.user`, `req.client`, `req.cleaner`
 *
 * For now we accept headers:
 *   x-user-role: "client" | "cleaner" | "admin"
 *   x-user-id: some-id
 */
export interface AuthedRequest extends Request {
  user?: {
    id: string;
    role: "client" | "cleaner" | "admin";
  };
}

export function authMiddleware(req: AuthedRequest, res: Response, next: NextFunction) {
  const role = (req.header("x-user-role") as any) || null;
  const id = req.header("x-user-id") || null;

  if (!role || !id) {
    return res.status(401).json({ error: { code: "UNAUTHENTICATED", message: "Missing auth headers" } });
  }

  if (!["client", "cleaner", "admin"].includes(role)) {
    return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "INVALID_ROLE", message: "Invalid role" } });
  }

  req.user = { id, role };
  next();
}
""")

# src/routes/jobs.ts
write("src/routes/jobs.ts", """
import { Router } from "express";
import { z } from "zod";
import { query } from "../db/client";
import { authMiddleware, AuthedRequest } from "../middleware/auth";
import { applyJobEvent, getJob } from "../services/jobsService";
import type { JobStatus } from "../state/jobStateMachine";

export const jobsRouter = Router();

// Create job (client)
jobsRouter.post("/", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "client") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only clients can create jobs" } });
    }

    const schema = z.object({
      scheduled_start: z.string(),
      estimated_hours: z.number(),
      total_credits: z.number()
    });

    const body = schema.parse(req.body);

    const result = await query(
      `
      INSERT INTO jobs (client_id, status, scheduled_start, estimated_hours, total_credits)
      VALUES ($1, 'requested', $2, $3, $4)
      RETURNING *;
      `,
      [req.user.id, body.scheduled_start, body.estimated_hours, body.total_credits]
    );

    const job = result.rows[0];

    // Also emit job.created event
    await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: "none",
      eventName: "job.created",
      payload: {},
      clientId: req.user.id
    });

    res.status(201).json({ job });
  } catch (err: any) {
    console.error("POST /jobs error", err);
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_CREATE_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Get job
jobsRouter.get("/:id", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    const job = await getJob(req.params.id);
    if (!job) {
      return res.status(404).json({ error: { code: "JOB_NOT_FOUND", message: "Job not found" } });
    }
    res.json({ job });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(500).json({ error: { code: "JOB_FETCH_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Helper to load and basic permission check
async function loadJobForAction(req: AuthedRequest, res: any) {
  const job = await getJob(req.params.id);
  if (!job) {
    res.status(404).json({ error: { code: "JOB_NOT_FOUND", message: "Job not found" } });
    return null;
  }
  // Basic role-based access: in real system you'd check job.client_id / cleaner_id
  return job;
}

// Cleaner accepts job
jobsRouter.post("/:id/accept", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "cleaner") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only cleaners can accept jobs" } });
    }
    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_accepted",
      payload: {},
      cleanerId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_ACCEPT_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Cleaner on my way
jobsRouter.post("/:id/on-my-way", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "cleaner") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only cleaners can update this job" } });
    }

    const schema = z.object({
      gps_lat: z.number(),
      gps_lng: z.number()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body);

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_on_my_way",
      payload: body,
      cleanerId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_ON_MY_WAY_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Cleaner check-in
jobsRouter.post("/:id/check-in", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "cleaner") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only cleaners can check in" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      gps_lat: z.number(),
      gps_lng: z.number()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body);

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_checked_in",
      payload: body,
      cleanerId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_CHECK_IN_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Cleaner check-out
jobsRouter.post("/:id/check-out", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "cleaner") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only cleaners can check out" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      gps_lat: z.number(),
      gps_lng: z.number()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body);

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_checked_out",
      payload: body,
      cleanerId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_CHECK_OUT_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Cleaner submits for approval
jobsRouter.post("/:id/submit-for-approval", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "cleaner") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only cleaners can submit" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      notes: z.string().optional(),
      photos: z.array(z.string()).optional()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body ?? {});

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval",
      payload: body,
      cleanerId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_SUBMIT_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Client approves
jobsRouter.post("/:id/approve", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "client") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only clients can approve" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      rating: z.number().min(1).max(5).optional(),
      feedback: z.string().optional()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body ?? {});

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.client_approved",
      payload: body,
      clientId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_APPROVE_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Client disputes
jobsRouter.post("/:id/dispute", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (req.user?.role !== "client") {
      return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Only clients can dispute" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      reason: z.string(),
      photos: z.array(z.string()).optional()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body);

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.client_disputed",
      payload: body,
      clientId: req.user.id
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_DISPUTE_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});

// Cancel job (client or cleaner)
jobsRouter.post("/:id/cancel", authMiddleware, async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  try {
    if (!req.user) {
      return res.status(401).json({ error: { code: "UNAUTHENTICATED", message: "Auth required" } });
    }
    const schema = z.object({
      reason: z.string().optional()
    });
    const body = schema.parse(req.body ?? {});

    const job = await loadJobForAction(req, res);
    if (!job) return;

    const payload = {
      ...body,
      cancelled_by: req.user.role
    };

    const { nextStatus, event } = await applyJobEvent({
      jobId: job.id,
      currentStatus: job.status as JobStatus,
      eventName: "job.cancelled",
      payload,
      clientId: req.user.role === "client" ? req.user.id : undefined,
      cleanerId: req.user.role === "cleaner" ? req.user.id : undefined
    });

    res.json({ status: nextStatus, event });
  } catch (err: any) {
    res.status(400).json({ error: { code: "JOB_CANCEL_FAILED", message: err.message ?? "Unknown error" } });
  }
});
""")

# src/routes/health.ts
write("src/routes/health.ts", """
import { Router } from "express";
export const healthRouter = Router();

healthRouter.get("/", (_req, res) => {
  res.json({ ok: true, service: "puretask-backend", time: new Date().toISOString() });
});
""")

# src/routes/admin.ts
write("src/routes/admin.ts", """
import { Router } from "express";
import { query } from "../db/client";
import { authMiddleware, AuthedRequest } from "../middleware/auth";

export const adminRouter = Router();

adminRouter.use(authMiddleware);

adminRouter.get("/jobs", async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  if (req.user?.role !== "admin") {
    return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Admin only" } });
  }
  const result = await query("SELECT * FROM jobs ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 100");
  res.json({ jobs: result.rows });
});

adminRouter.get("/job-events", async (req: AuthedRequest, res) => {
  if (req.user?.role !== "admin") {
    return res.status(403).json({ error: { code: "FORBIDDEN", message: "Admin only" } });
  }
  const result = await query("SELECT * FROM job_events ORDER BY occurred_at DESC LIMIT 200");
  res.json({ events: result.rows });
});
""")

# src/index.ts
write("src/index.ts", """
import express from "express";
import cors from "cors";
import { env } from "./config/env";
import { jobsRouter } from "./routes/jobs";
import { healthRouter } from "./routes/health";
import { adminRouter } from "./routes/admin";

const app = express();

app.use(cors());
app.use(express.json());

app.use("/health", healthRouter);
app.use("/jobs", jobsRouter);
app.use("/admin", adminRouter);

app.use((err: any, _req: express.Request, res: express.Response, _next: express.NextFunction) => {
  console.error("[unhandled-error]", err);
  res.status(500).json({ error: { code: "INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR", message: "Unexpected error" } });
});

app.listen(env.PORT, () => {
  console.log(`PureTask backend listening on port ${env.PORT}`);
});
""")

# Dockerfile
write("Dockerfile", """
FROM node:20-alpine

WORKDIR /app

COPY package.json package-lock.json* yarn.lock* pnpm-lock.yaml* .npmrc* ./ 2>/dev/null || true
RUN npm install

COPY . .

RUN npm run build

EXPOSE 4000

CMD ["npm", "start"]
""")

# README
write("README.md", """
# PureTask Backend (v0.1)

This is a minimal but real backend for PureTask, built with:

- Node.js + TypeScript
- Express
- PostgreSQL (Neon)
- A job lifecycle state machine
- Job event emitter that writes to `job_events`

## Quick start

1. Create a `.env` file in the project root:

   DATABASE_URL=postgres://user:password@host:port/dbname
   PORT=4000

2. Install dependencies:

   npm install

3. Run in dev mode:

   npm run dev

4. Hit the health endpoint:

   GET http://localhost:4000/health

## Auth (temporary)

For now, auth is simulated with HTTP headers:

- `x-user-role`: `client` | `cleaner` | `admin`
- `x-user-id`: any string

Later you can swap this with Clerk, Supabase Auth, or your own JWT.

## Main endpoints

- `POST /jobs` (client) – create a job
- `GET /jobs/:id` – fetch a job
- `POST /jobs/:id/accept` (cleaner)
- `POST /jobs/:id/on-my-way` (cleaner)
- `POST /jobs/:id/check-in` (cleaner)
- `POST /jobs/:id/check-out` (cleaner)
- `POST /jobs/:id/submit-for-approval` (cleaner)
- `POST /jobs/:id/approve` (client)
- `POST /jobs/:id/dispute` (client)
- `POST /jobs/:id/cancel` (client/cleaner)

Each action:

1. Validates the request body with `zod`.
2. Applies the job state machine (`src/state/jobStateMachine.ts`).
3. Updates the `jobs.status` column.
4. Inserts a row into `job_events`.

## Admin API

- `GET /admin/jobs` – list recent jobs (role: admin)
- `GET /admin/job-events` – list recent job events (role: admin)

Use header:

- `x-user-role: admin`
- `x-user-id: admin-1`

## Docker

To build and run:

```bash
docker build -t puretask-backend .
docker run -p 4000:4000 --env-file .env puretask-backend
Make sure your Neon DATABASE_URL is reachable from the container.
""")

Zip it
zip_path = "/mnt/data/puretask-backend.zip"
with zipfile.ZipFile(zip_path, "w", zipfile.ZIP_DEFLATED) as z:
for root, dirs, files in os.walk(base_dir):
for f in files:
full = os.path.join(root, f)
rel = os.path.relpath(full, base_dir)
z.write(full, rel)

zip_path

Result
'/mnt/data/puretask-backend.zip'
Nice, ok — I’ve generated a first real backend for you as a zip. You can grab it here:

➡️ Download puretask-backend.zip

Here’s what you’ve got and how it fits together.

What this backend includes
1. Tech stack
Node.js + TypeScript

Express HTTP API

PostgreSQL (Neon) via DATABASE_URL

Zod for request validation

Simple state-machine for job lifecycle

job_events emitter that writes directly to your job_events table

Basic Admin API to inspect jobs and events

File / folder overview
Root
package.json

Scripts:

npm run dev – dev server with auto-reload

npm run build – compile TypeScript

npm start – run compiled JS

tsconfig.json – TS compiler settings

Dockerfile

Builds and runs the API on port 4000

README.md

Quickstart instructions

You’ll also create your own .env (not included):

DATABASE_URL=postgres://USER:PASSWORD@HOST:PORT/DBNAME
PORT=4000
NODE_ENV=development
src/config/env.ts
Loads env variables with dotenv:

DATABASE_URL – Neon connection string

PORT – API port (default 4000)

Warns you if DATABASE_URL is missing.

src/db/client.ts
Postgres connection wrapper:

Creates a Pool using DATABASE_URL

Exports a helper:

export async function query<T = any>(text: string, params?: any[]): Promise<{ rows: T[] }>
You’ll use this everywhere to talk to Neon.

src/state/jobStateMachine.ts
Your job lifecycle brain.

Defines allowed JobStatus values:

"requested" | "accepted" | "on_my_way" | "in_progress" |
"awaiting_approval" | "completed" | "disputed" |
"cancelled" | "no_show"
Defines JobEventName:

"job.created"
"job.cleaner_accepted"
"job.cleaner_on_my_way"
"job.cleaner_checked_in"
"job.cleaner_checked_out"
"job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval"
"job.client_approved"
"job.client_disputed"
"job.cancelled"
Has a transition table and a helper:

getNextStatus(current: JobStatus | "none", event: JobEventName): JobStatus | null
If a transition is illegal, it returns null and the endpoint will throw.

src/services/eventsService.ts
Responsible for writing to job_events:

export async function publishEvent({
  jobId,
  eventName,
  payload,
  cleanerId,
  clientId,
  source = "backend",
  occurredAt = new Date()
})
Inserts into job_events with payload::jsonb

Returns the inserted event row

This matches the table structure you showed (id, job_id, event_name, payload, cleaner_id, client_id, source, occurred_at, created_at).

src/services/jobsService.ts
Central logic for updating jobs + emitting events.

Key pieces:

getJob(jobId) – fetches a job row from jobs

applyJobEvent({...}):

Uses getNextStatus(currentStatus, eventName)

If invalid → throws INVALID_STATUS_TRANSITION

UPDATE jobs SET status = nextStatus, cleaner_id = COALESCE($3, cleaner_id)

Calls publishEvent(...) to insert into job_events

Returns { nextStatus, event }

You may need to tweak columns here depending on your final jobs schema, but it’s wired to the basics (id, status, cleaner_id, updated_at).

src/middleware/auth.ts
Temporary fake auth so you can call endpoints immediately.

Looks for headers:

x-user-role: client | cleaner | admin
x-user-id: some-string
Attaches:

req.user = { id, role }
Rejects if missing/invalid ⇒ 401/403

Later, this is where you’ll plug Clerk / Supabase Auth / JWT, but you can already test everything now with just headers.

src/routes/jobs.ts
This is the big one: all job lifecycle endpoints.

All routes use:

authMiddleware (so we know user role/id)

zod schemas to validate the body

getJob() to fetch

applyJobEvent() to:

enforce the state machine

update jobs.status

insert into job_events

Endpoints:

POST /jobs (client)

Body: scheduled_start, estimated_hours, total_credits

Inserts a jobs row with status = 'requested'

Then calls applyJobEvent with job.created (from "none" → "requested")

GET /jobs/:id

Returns job details

POST /jobs/:id/accept (cleaner)

Emits job.cleaner_accepted

Updates status via state machine: requested → accepted

POST /jobs/:id/on-my-way (cleaner)

Body: gps_lat, gps_lng

Emits job.cleaner_on_my_way

Status: accepted → on_my_way

POST /jobs/:id/check-in (cleaner)

Body: gps_lat, gps_lng

Emits job.cleaner_checked_in

Status: accepted/on_my_way → in_progress

POST /jobs/:id/check-out (cleaner)

Body: gps_lat, gps_lng

Emits job.cleaner_checked_out

Status stays in_progress (as per v1 plan)

POST /jobs/:id/submit-for-approval (cleaner)

Body: notes?, photos?: string[]

Emits job.cleaner_submitted_for_approval

Status: in_progress → awaiting_approval

POST /jobs/:id/approve (client)

Body: rating?, feedback?

Emits job.client_approved

Status: awaiting_approval → completed

POST /jobs/:id/dispute (client)

Body: reason, photos?

Emits job.client_disputed

Status: awaiting_approval → disputed

POST /jobs/:id/cancel (client or cleaner)

Body: reason?

Adds cancelled_by = req.user.role into payload

Emits job.cancelled

Status: requested/accepted/... → cancelled (depending on current)

Each route returns { status: nextStatus, event } or a clear error object.

src/routes/admin.ts
Mini PureTask Admin Dashboard API (for now, JSON only):

All routes require x-user-role: admin

GET /admin/jobs – recent jobs (LIMIT 100, ordered DESC)

GET /admin/job-events – recent events (LIMIT 200)

This is what your admin UI (or n8n, or a quick React dashboard) can call to inspect the system.

src/routes/health.ts
GET /health – simple “I’m alive” JSON.

src/index.ts
Main server bootstrap:

Sets up Express, CORS, JSON body parser

Mounts:

/health

/jobs

/admin

Global error handler

Listens on PORT (default 4000)

How to run it locally (step-by-step)

Unzip it somewhere on your machine.

Create .env in the project root

DATABASE_URL=your_neon_connection_string_here
PORT=4000

cd puretask-backend
npm install

npm run dev
Test health
