How to test a full job lifecycle
Use something like Postman, Insomnia, or curl. Remember the auth headers:

x-user-role: client
x-user-id: client-1
Create job (client)

POST http://localhost:4000/jobs

Headers:

x-user-role: client

x-user-id: client-1

Content-Type: application/json

Body:

{
  "scheduled_start": "2025-12-01T10:00:00Z",
  "estimated_hours": 3,
  "total_credits": 50
}
Response will contain job.id.

Accept as cleaner

POST /jobs/:id/accept with:

x-user-role: cleaner

x-user-id: cleaner-1

On my way → check-in → submit → approve, etc.

Each step will:

Enforce the state machine

Update jobs.status

Insert a row into job_events

You can confirm in Neon with:

SELECT * FROM jobs ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 5;
SELECT * FROM job_events ORDER BY occurred_at DESC LIMIT 10;
If you’d like, next we can:

Wire n8n to this backend (instead of direct DB writes), or

Add real auth (Clerk or Supabase) to replace the header-based stub, or

Add Stripe payment intent creation + linking jobs to payment_intents.




   ALL THIS LOOKS GREAT AND I WANNA USE EVERYTHING BUT I DONT KNOW HOW TO IMPLEMENT ANYTHING FROM YOUR PREVIOUS OUTPUT

Totally fair. Let’s slow it down and just walk through exactly what to click and type so this thing actually runs for you.

We’ll ignore Docker, GitHub, “advanced” stuff for now. Just:

Get backend running on your laptop + talking to your Neon DB.

0️⃣ What you already have
A ready-made backend zip:
➡️ Download puretask-backend.zip

Neon database with:

jobs

job_events

stripe_events

payment_intents

All we’re doing now is connecting this backend to that Neon DB and running it.

1️⃣ One-time setup on your computer
1. Make sure Node.js is installed
On your computer, open a terminal (or Command Prompt) and run:

node -v
npm -v
If both show a version (like v20.x and 10.x), you’re good.

If not, install Node from the official site (nodejs.org) – then rerun those two commands.

2️⃣ Get the backend folder on your machine
Click this:
➡️ puretask-backend.zip
Save it somewhere easy (like Desktop or Documents).

Unzip it

Right click → “Extract All…” (Windows)

Or double-click (Mac) and it makes a folder like puretask-backend.

You should now have a folder like:

puretask-backend/
  package.json
  tsconfig.json
  Dockerfile
  README.md
  src/
    index.ts
    routes/
    services/
    ...
3️⃣ Connect it to your Neon database
We need your Neon connection string.

1. Get DATABASE_URL from Neon
In the Neon dashboard:

Go to your project

Click “Connect”

Copy the connection string that looks like:

postgresql://USER:PASSWORD@HOST:PORT/DBNAME
Keep that copied.

2. Create a .env file in the backend folder
In the puretask-backend folder, create a new file called .env (no name, just .env):

Put this inside:

DATABASE_URL=postgresql://USER:PASSWORD@HOST:PORT/DBNAME
PORT=4000
NODE_ENV=development
Replace the DATABASE_URL with the one you copied from Neon.

Save the file.

4️⃣ Install dependencies & run the backend
Open a terminal inside the puretask-backend folder:

On Mac: right-click folder → “New Terminal at Folder”

On Windows: Shift + right-click → “Open PowerShell window here” (or use VS Code terminal)

Then run:

npm install
Let it finish (first time will take a bit).

Then run:

npm run dev
If everything is good, you should see:

PureTask backend listening on port 4000
That means your backend is live at:

http://localhost:4000

5️⃣ Test that it works (health endpoint)
Open a browser and go to:

http://localhost:4000/health

You should see JSON like:

{
  "ok": true,
  "service": "puretask-backend",
  "time": "2025-..."
}
If you see that, the backend is up and talking.

6️⃣ Test a real job flow (with dummy headers)
Let’s hit a real endpoint now so you can see it talk to Neon.

Use Postman, Insomnia, or a REST client. If you don’t have any, you can even use the VS Code REST client extension later, but I’ll describe Postman-style:

A. Create a job (client)
Request:

Method: POST

URL: http://localhost:4000/jobs

Headers:

Content-Type: application/json

x-user-role: client

x-user-id: client-1

Body (JSON):

{
  "scheduled_start": "2025-12-01T10:00:00Z",
  "estimated_hours": 3,
  "total_credits": 50
}
Send it.
